Belief in Specific Angels: Individuals and Types
Dardeer enumerates the individual angels and types that require detailed belief.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the major individual angels and the types of angels mentioned in revelation, including their roles.

Core Idea
Revelation names specific angels and types, each with a unique role in Allah's creation.

After establishing the general obligation to believe in angels, Dardeer now details the specific angels we must know individually, such as Jibril and Israfil, and the types of angels we must believe in, such as the guardians and recorders. This lesson covers the names and functions of these noble beings, grounding each in Qur'anic proof.

Guided Path
1
List the chief angels by name
Dardeer names Jibril, Israfil, Mika'il, 'Azra'il, Munkar, Nakir, Ridwan, and Malik. Note that these are the well-known individuals. Understand their roles if known (e.g., Jibril brings revelation, Israfil blows the Trumpet).
The first four are often called the archangels.
2
Understand belief 'by type'
Believing in types means accepting that there are categories like the bearers of the Throne, assistants to 'Azra'il, guardian angels (ḥafaza), and recording angels (kataba).
The passage gives specific details about guardians and recorders.
3
Study the guardian and recording angels
Guardians protect humans from harm, even children and disbelievers, as per Qur'an 13:11. Recording angels write all deeds, never leaving except in specific states; they are two angels named Raqib and 'Atid (Qur'an 50:17-18).
This shows the comprehensive nature of divine accounting.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) بوجودِ (الأمْلاكِ) وعِصْمتهم أيضًا، قال تعالى: ﴿وَلَا يَعْصُونَ اللَّهَ مَا أَمَرَهُمْ وَيَفْعَلُونَ مَا يُؤْمَرُونَ﴾، جمعُ ملَكٍ، وهو: جسم لطيفٌ رُوحاني نوراني له القدرة على التشكلات الجميلة. ويجب الإيمان بهم إجمالا فيمن عُلِمَ منهم إجمالا، وتفصيلا فيمن عُلِمَ منهم تفصيلا: بالشخص؛ كجبريل وإسرافيل وميكائيل وعزرائيل، وهُم رُؤساء الملائكة عليهم الصلاة والسلام أجمعين، ومُنكر ونكير، ورضوان خازن الجنان، ومالك خازن النيران. أو بالنَّوع كحَمَلة العرش، وأعوان السيّدِ عِزرائيل، والحفظة: ملائكة وهم مُوَكِّلون بحفظ البشَر - ولو صغيرًا وكافرًا - مِنَ الجنّ مَثَلًا، قال تعالى: ﴿لَهُ مُعَقِّبَاتٌ مِّن بَيْنِ يَدَيْهِ وَمِنْ خَلْفِهِ يَحْفَظُونَهُ مِنْ أَمْرِ اللهِ﴾، والكتبة: وهم ملائكة يكتبون على المكلف جميع ما صدَرَ منه مِنْ قَولٍ ولو نفْسيًّا وفعل واعتقاد، لا يُفارقونه إلا في حالة الجماع والغُسلِ والخلاء، والمشهور أنها ملكان يُسمّى أحدُهُما الرقيب والثاني العتيد، كما في سورة ق.
(And) [belief] in the existence of (the angels) and their infallibility as well, He said exalted: "And they do not disobey Allah in what He commands them and they do what they are commanded" (Qur'an 66:6). They are the plural of malak, and he is: a subtle, spiritual, luminous body having ability for beautiful transformations. And it is obligatory to believe in them generally regarding whom is known generally, and in detail regarding whom is known in detail: by individual; like Jibril, Israfil, Mika'il, and 'Azra'il, and they are the chiefs of the angels, peace and blessings be upon them all, and Munkar and Nakir, and Ridwan the keeper of Paradise, and Malik the keeper of Hellfire. Or by type, like the bearers of the Throne, and the assistants of sayyid 'Azra'il, and the guardians: angels who are entrusted with guarding humans—even if a child or a disbeliever—from jinn for example, He said exalted: "For him are successive [angels] before him and behind him who guard him by the command of Allah" (Qur'an 13:11), and the writers: and they are angels who write upon the morally responsible all that issues from him of speech, even inner, and action, and belief; they do not leave him except during intercourse, ritual bath, and relieving oneself, and the well-known is that they are two angels, one called ar-Raqib and the second 'Atid, as in Surat Qaf.
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage addresses the obligation to believe in angels, their infallibility, and the categories of belief. It begins by stating the obligation to believe in the existence of angels and their 'isma (infallibility), citing Qur'an 66:6 which states they do not disobey Allah. It then provides a definition of an angel (malak): a subtle (laṭif), spiritual (rūḥānī), luminous (nūrānī) body with the power of beautiful transformations. The next part distinguishes two levels of obligatory belief: general belief in those known generally, and detailed belief in those known in detail. Detailed belief is further divided: by individual (bi-l-shakhṣ), listing specific angels like Jibril, Israfil, Mika'il, 'Azra'il, Munkar, Nakir, Ridwan, and Malik; and by type (bi-l-naw'), giving examples such as the bearers of the Throne, assistants of 'Azra'il, the guardian angels (ḥafaza) who protect humans, citing Qur'an 13:11, and the recording angels (kataba) who write all deeds of every accountable person, with a note about when they leave. It mentions the well-known view that there are two recording angels named Raqib and 'Atid, referencing Surah Qaf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe there is only one guardian angel or that angels do not record inner thoughts.
Correction: The passage states that the recording angels write even inner speech (qawl nafsī) and that there are multiple guardians (ḥafaza).

Checkpoint
According to Dardeer, which angels are entrusted with guarding humans?
A) The kataba (writers)
B) The ḥamalat al-ʿarsh (bearers of the Throne)
C) The ḥafaza (guardians)
D) The assistants of 'Azra'il

Key Takeaway
Belief in angels requires knowing the named individuals and the types, such as guardians and recorders, each with distinct functions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The angels record even your inner speech—the words you say to yourself. What do you say to yourself most often, and are those words worthy of being preserved forever? Will you commit today to replacing one self-critical thought with a remembrance of Allah?
?
The guardians protect you from harm you never see. When was the last time you thanked Allah for a danger averted that you didn't even notice? How can you cultivate a heart of gratitude for His hidden protection?
?
You are never alone; two angels are with you except in private moments. Does this awareness increase your mindfulness of sin, or has it grown stale? What one habit can you change to live with greater consciousness of their presence?

Belief in Angels: Nature, Categories, and Roles
Dardeer explains the obligation to believe in angels, their nature, and categories.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic belief in angels, including their nature as luminous spiritual bodies, the obligation to believe in them generally and specifically, and the categories of angels mentioned in revelation.

Core Idea
Angels are luminous spiritual beings created by Allah to execute His commands without disobedience.

This passage from Imam Dardeer's Sharh al-Kharidah establishes the core doctrines regarding angels. It defines their nature, emphasizes the obligation to believe in them, and provides a detailed classification of the angels known to us by name and type. Understanding these categories helps Muslims appreciate the unseen world that interacts with our own.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of an angel
Begin by reading the Arabic definition: angel is a subtle, spiritual, luminous body with power to assume forms. Note the three adjectives: subtle, spiritual, luminous.
This definition is key to distinguishing angels from other beings.
2
Distinguish general vs. specific belief
The passage states we must believe in angels generally and specifically. Identify which angels are known by person and which by type.
3
Explore the roles of guardian and scribe angels
Read the section about the hafaza (guardians) and kataba (scribes). Note their functions: protection and recording deeds.
Guardians protect from jinn; scribes record every action.
4
Consider the recording angels debate
The passage mentions different opinions on whether the two recording angels are fixed or change daily. Understand the dominant view that they are two angels named Raqib and 'Atid.
There is also an opinion that they alternate daily.
5
Summarize the essential belief
Conclude with the 'in summary' part: every human has guardians and scribes in a general sense.
We don't need to know the specifics of location or identity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و) بوجودِ (الأمْلاكِ) وعِصْمتهم ) أيضًا ، قال تعالى: ﴿وَلَا يَعْصُونَ اللَّهَ مَا أَمَرَهُمْ وَيَفْعَلُونَ مَا يُؤْمَرُونَ﴾ (٢)، جمعُ ملَكٍ»، وهو: جسم لطيفٌ رُوحاني نوراني له القدرة على التشكلات الجميلة. ويجب الإيمان بهم إجمالا فيمن عُلِمَ منهم إجمالا، وتفصيلا فيمن عُلِمَ منهم تفصيلا: - بالشخص؛ كجبريل وإسرافيل وميكائيل وعزرائيل، وهُم رؤساء الملائكة عليهم الصلاة والسلام أجمعين، ومُنكر ونكير (۳)، ورضوان خازن الجنان، ومالك خازن النيران. - أو بالنَّوع كحَمَلة العرش (4) ، وأعوان السيّدِ عِزرائيل، والحفظة: ملائكة وهم مُوَكِّلون بحفظ البشَر - ولو صغيرًا وكافرًا - مِنَ الجنّ مَثَلًا، قال تعالى: ﴿لَهُ مُعَقِّبَاتٌ مِّن بَيْنِ يَدَيْهِ وَمِنْ خَلْفِهِ يَحْفَظُونَهُ مِنْ (٥) أَمْرِ اللهِ )، والكتبة: وهم ملائكة يكتبونَ على المكلف جميع ما صدَرَ منه مِنْ قَولٍ ولو نفْسيًّا وفعل واعتقاد، لا يُفارقونه إلا في حالة الجماع والغُسلِ والخلاء)، والمشهور أنها ملكان (۸) يُسمّى أحدُهُما الرقيب والثاني العتيد، كما في سورة ق. ولكُلِّ يَوم وليلة ملكان يتعاقبان عند صلاة العصْرِ وصلاة الصبح، وقيل: بل هما تكان فقط لا يتغيّران ما دامَ حيا، وإذا مات جلسا على قبره يستغْفَرانِ له، أي: إن كانَ مُؤمِنًا. ومحلها مِنَ الإنسان عاتقاه (۲) ، وقيل : ذَقَنُه، وقيل: شفَتاه، وقيلَ: عُنقه، وقيل : الناجذان (۳) ، وقيل : إنَّ الكتبة همُ الحفظة. وبالجملة الواجب اعتقاده، أنَّ على الإنسان حفظةً وكتبةً على سبيل الإجمال.
And (belief in) the existence of the angels and their infallibility also, He said the Exalted: {They do not disobey Allah what He commands them and they do what they are commanded} (2). The plural of 'malak', which is a subtle spiritual luminous body having the power to assume beautiful forms. And it is obligatory to believe in them in general regarding those known in general, and in detail regarding those known in detail: - by person, such as Jibril, Israfil, Mika'il, and 'Azra'il, and they are the chief angels, peace and blessings be upon them all, and Munkar and Nakir (3), and Ridwan the keeper of Paradise, and Malik the keeper of Hellfire. - Or by type, such as the bearers of the Throne (4), and the assistants of Sayyid 'Azra'il, and the guardians: angels who are entrusted with protecting humans – even a child or a disbeliever – from the jinn for example. He said the Exalted: {For him are successive angels before him and behind him, protecting him from (5) the command of Allah}, and the scribes: they are angels who write upon the morally responsible all that issues from him of speech, even inward, and action and belief; they do not leave him except in the state of sexual intercourse, ritual washing, and relieving oneself, and the well-known view is that they are two angels (8) called one of them Raqib and the other 'Atid, as in Surat Qaf. And for every day and night there are two angels who alternate at the 'Asr prayer and the Fajr prayer, and it is said: rather they are two angels only who do not change as long as he lives, and when he dies they sit at his grave seeking forgiveness for him, i.e. if he is a believer. And their place on the human is his shoulders (2), and it is said: his chin, and it is said: his lips, and it is said: his neck, and it is said: the two molars (3), and it is said: the scribes are the guardians. And in summary, what must be believed is that upon the human there are guardians and scribes in a general way.
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage explains the obligation to believe in angels and provides details about their nature and categories. It begins by defining an angel as a subtle, spiritual, luminous body capable of assuming beautiful forms. It then states that belief in angels is obligatory both in general (for those known only in general terms) and in detail (for those known by name or specific type). The passage lists angels known by person: Jibril, Israfil, Mika'il, 'Azra'il (the archangels), along with Munkar and Nakir (the angels of the grave), Ridwan (keeper of Paradise), and Malik (keeper of Hell). It then mentions categories known by type, such as the bearers of the Throne, the assistants of 'Azra'il, the guardian angels (hafaza), who protect humans, and the scribe angels (kataba), who record every speech, action, and belief of the morally responsible. Special attention is given to the recording angels: the dominant view is that they are two types (not individuals) named Raqib and 'Atid. The passage also notes that two angels alternate daily at certain prayers, and when a person dies, they sit at the grave seeking forgiveness. Various opinions are given about the location of these angels on the body. The passage concludes that the essential belief is that every human has guardian and scribe angels in a general sense.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The two recording angels are fixed individuals that never change throughout a person's life and are the same every day.
Correction: The dominant view names them Raqib and 'Atid, but there is also an opinion that two angels alternate daily at Asr and Fajr prayers. After death, they become the grave angels seeking forgiveness. Their location on the body is also debated. The essential belief is that guardians and scribes exist in general.

Checkpoint
What is the nature of angels according to this passage?
A) They are pure spirits with no bodies.
B) They are luminous spiritual bodies capable of assuming forms.
C) They are physical bodies like humans.
D) They are imaginary beings.

Key Takeaway
Belief in angels is an integral part of Iman, and we affirm their existence as luminous spiritual beings with specific roles including recording and protecting humans.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have two angels recording every word you speak, even those muttered to yourself. What will you start saying today that you want written in your book of deeds, and what will you stop saying?
?
If you truly believed that guardian angels are constantly protecting you from harm you cannot see, how would your daily worries change? What is one fear you will hand over to Allah after reading this lesson?
?
The passage teaches that angels never disobey Allah. Look at your own obedience: which command of Allah have you been ignoring or delaying? What concrete step will you take within the next hour to begin obeying it fully?

Belief in the Guardian Angels (Hafaza)
Dardeer presents various reports about the recording angels and states the minimal obligatory belief.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that belief in the recording angels is obligatory in general terms, without needing to know specific details about their number, alternation, or location on the body.

Core Idea
Belief in the guardian angels is obligatory in general; details are not required.

This passage from Imam Dardeer's commentary addresses the sam'iyyat (matters known from revelation) regarding the angels who record deeds. While there are various reported opinions about their number, alternation, and location, the author emphasizes that the essential belief is simply that every person has guardians and writers. This lesson will clarify what must be believed and what is left to scholarly discussion.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get an overview. Then read the literal translation. Notice the different reports mentioned.
Pay attention to the variety of opinions, as the author mentions multiple views before giving the conclusion.
2
Identify the different reports
List the various opinions: alternation at Asr and Fajr, permanence, grave sitting, location on the body, and the identity of writers as guardians.
This shows the range of transmitted reports in the tradition.
3
Find the author's conclusion
The author says 'وبالجملة الواجب اعتقاده...' (In summary, the obligatory belief...). This is the key point: general belief without detailed specification.
This reflects the Ash'ari principle of accepting revelation in general terms.
4
Reflect on the principle of 'ijmal
Consider why the author does not require belief in any particular detail. In sam'iyyat, many specifics are not essential for faith.
This helps avoid unnecessary theological disputes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وليلة ملكان يتعاقبان عند صلاة العصْرِ وصلاة الصبح، وقيل: بل هما تكان فقط لا يتغيّران ما دامَ حيا، وإذا مات جلسا على قبره يستغْفَرانِ له، أي: إن كانَ مُؤمِنًا. ومحلها مِنَ الإنسان عاتقاه، وقيل: ذَقَنُه، وقيل: شفَتاه، وقيلَ: عُنقه، وقيل: الناجذان، وقيل: إنَّ الكتبة همُ الحفظة. وبالجملة الواجب اعتقاده، أنَّ على الإنسان حفظةً وكتبةً على سبيل الإجمال.
And for every night two angels alternate at the prayer of Asr and the prayer of Fajr. And it is said: rather they are two permanent ones, not changing as long as one is alive. And when one dies, they sit on his grave seeking forgiveness for him, that is, if he was a believer. And their place in the human is his collarbones; and it is said: his chin; and it is said: his lips; and it is said: his neck; and it is said: the two wisdom teeth. And it is said: the writers are the guardians. And in summary, what must be believed is that there are guardians and writers for a human being in general terms.
Source pages p. 156

Commentary
This passage discusses the sam'iyyat (audible matters) concerning the angels who record deeds. Dardeer begins by mentioning a view that two angels alternate for each day and night, coming at Asr and Fajr prayers. Another view holds they are two fixed angels who do not change while the person lives. After death, they sit on the grave and seek forgiveness for a believer. Their location on the human body is disputed: some say on the collarbones (عَاتِقَاه), others on the chin, lips, neck, or wisdom teeth (النَّاجِذَان). Then he reconciles by saying that the writers (الكاتبة) are the guardians (الحفظة). The essential obligatory belief is that there are guardians and writers for every person, but detailed specifics are not required. This reflects the Ash'ari principle of takhsis in matters of sam'iyyat: one must affirm what is established in general and leave details to the revealed texts.

Key Terms
الحفظة
الكتبة
العاتق
الناجذان
السمعيات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people think that they must know the exact number, names, and physical location of the recording angels as part of their faith.
Correction: The passage clarifies that the obligatory belief is only the general existence of these angels; the specific details are not required for faith and may be left to scholarly interpretation.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the essential belief regarding the angels?
A) That they are exactly two angels per day.
B) That they sit on the grave only after death.
C) That there are guardians and writers for every person in general.
D) That their location is definitely the collarbones.

Key Takeaway
The obligatory belief about the recording angels is that they exist for every person, without requiring knowledge of their specific nature or location.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You believe the guardian angels are with you now, recording your every word and deed. Are there words you have spoken today that you would be ashamed to see in your record? Right now, silently repent for one such word and resolve to speak only what is good for the rest of the day.
?
The angels seek forgiveness for the believer after death. Are you living a life that gives them something to seek forgiveness for? Think of one sin you keep repeating. Make a firm intention to stop, and ask Allah to help you, because your angels are watching.
?
You now know that you do not need to know the details of the angels. Does your heart find peace in that, or does your mind still crave control? Surrender the need to know 'how' and simply act with awareness that you are never alone—let this awareness change one action you are about to do.

The Number of Prophets: Certainty vs. Conjecture
Dardir explains why the exact number of prophets is not specified and the status of relevant hadiths.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Imam Dardir advises against specifying the exact number of prophets and the ruling on using solitary hadith reports in matters of belief.

Core Idea
Speculating on the exact number of prophets is both risky and unnecessary for faith.

Imam Dardir addresses a question that might occur to many students: Can we know exactly how many prophets there were? Drawing on a Quranic verse and the nature of hadith transmission, he explains why it is better to avoid a fixed number. This lesson unpacks his reasoning and its implications for Islamic theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the Quranic quote and the two hadith numbers.
2
Identify Dardir's two reasons
The passage gives two dangers of specifying a number: adding false prophets or excluding real ones. Find these in the text.
They are linked to the possibility of error in quantity.
3
Understand the hadith classification
Learn why the hadiths about the number are called 'khabar ahad' and why they do not yield certainty in 'aqidah.
Conjecture (zan) is not a valid basis for belief.
4
Reflect on the ruling
Consider why leaving the number unspecified is 'preferable' and how this protects the creed from error.
This connects to the broader principle of relying only on certain knowledge in beliefs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
منهم، والأولى ترْكُ حضرهم في عددٍ مُعيَّن؛ لقوله تعالى: مِنْهُم مَّن قَصَصْنَا عَلَيْكَ وَمِنْهُمْ مَّن لم نَقْصُص، ولا يؤمَنُ فِي ذِكْرِ العَدَدِ أنْ يُدْخَلَ فيهم مَنْ لَيسَ لَجَوازِ أَنْ يُذْكَرَ أكثَرُ مِنَ الواقع، أو يُخْرَجَ منهم مَن هو منهم إنْ كانَ العدَدُ أَقَلَّ . وما رُوِيَ أنَّ النبيَّ الله سُئِلَ عنْ عددهم فقال: (مائة ألف وأربعة وعشرون ألفًا)، وفي رواية (مائتا ألف وأربعة وعشرون ألفًا) فخبَرُ أَحاد لا يفيدُ القطع، ولا عبرة بالظَّنِّ في باب الاعتقادات.
Some of them, and the preferable thing is to leave specifying them in a definite number, because of His statement, may He be exalted: 'Among them are those We have related to you and among them are those We have not related [to you].' And it is not safe, when mentioning the number, that someone might be included who is not from them due to the possibility of mentioning more than the actual, or that someone who is from them might be excluded if the number is less. And what has been narrated that the Prophet, may God bless him and grant him peace, was asked about their number and he said: 'One hundred and twenty-four thousand,' and in another narration 'two hundred and twenty-four thousand,' is a khabar ahad (solitary report) which does not yield certainty, and there is no consideration for conjecture in matters of beliefs.
Source pages p. 157

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal argument about the number of prophets. Dardir begins by stating that it is preferable not to specify a definite number for the prophets, citing the Quranic verse (Ghafir 40:78) which indicates that some prophets are mentioned while others are not. He then gives two reasons: first, a number could be inflated to include non-prophets, and second, a number could be too small and exclude actual prophets. He then addresses the hadith reports giving specific numbers like 124,000 or 224,000, noting that these are khabar ahad (solitary reports), which do not provide certainty in matters of belief. Therefore, conjecture ('zan') is not reliable in 'aqidah.

Key Terms
عدد الأنبياء
خبر آحاد
الظن
الاعتقادات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the hadith numbers (124,000 or 224,000) are definitively established and part of Islamic creed.
Correction: These numbers come from solitary hadiths (khabar ahad) which do not produce certainty, and conjecture (zan) is not valid in matters of belief. Therefore, they are not part of 'aqidah.

Checkpoint
Why does Dardir say it is preferable not to specify a definite number for the prophets?
A) Because the Quran explicitly forbids it
B) To avoid including non-prophets or excluding actual prophets
C) Because there is no hadith on the number
D) Because the Companions disagreed

Key Takeaway
The exact number of prophets is unknown and irrelevant for Islamic belief; relying on weak hadiths for matters of creed is not permissible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your own life, are there religious beliefs or practices you hold that you have never verified against certain sources? How does this lesson on the number of prophets challenge you to examine the evidence for what you believe?
?
This lesson shows that even a well-known hadith can be insufficient for creed. Is there a belief you hold that might be based on a weak or solitary hadith? What would it cost you to investigate it?
?
The risk of error in specifying the number of prophets is that we might include or exclude someone wrongly. In your daily interactions, are you quick to judge who is 'in' or 'out' of Allah's mercy based on your own assumptions? How can this lesson teach you humility in such matters?

Belief in the Hoor of Paradise
Dardir defines the Hoor and their ocular characteristic.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition and description of the Hoor (houris) of Paradise as presented by Imam Dardir.

Core Idea
The Hoor are real beings with wide, intensely black-and-white eyes.

Imam Dardir moves from the sam'iyyat to specific details of Paradise. He begins with the Hoor, the women of Paradise, giving a precise physical description. This lesson unpacks that description and the obligation to believe in their existence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on Hoor
Read the Arabic passage about the Hoor once, then the translation. Notice the emphasis on the obligation to believe and the ocular description.
The term 'hawar' is defined lexically.
2
Analyze the ocular description
Focus on the definition of 'hawar': extreme whiteness of the eye with extreme blackness. Also note they are called 'in (wide-eyed). Why is this significant?
This physical description is taken literally.
3
Understand the doctrinal status
Recognize that belief in the Hoor is obligatory as part of the sam'iyyat (revealed matters). Reflect on why such details are emphasized.
Sam'iyyat are matters that must be accepted on divine authority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القسم الثالث: السمعيات (و) يجب الإيمان بوجودِ الحور جمع حوراء»، والحوَرُ: شِدَّةُ بياض العين مع شدة سوادها، وهُنَّ نساءُ الجَنَّةِ، وَوُصِفْنَ بِالعِينِ لانساعِ أَعْيُنِهِنَّ. (والولدان) أي: الغلمان، وهم على صورةِ عِلمانِ الدُّنيا، وهم خَدَمةُ أهل الجنّة. وقيل: إنهم أولادُ الكُفَّارِ الذين يموتون قبل البلوغ، فإنه ورَدَ أَنهم حَدَمةُ أَهْلَ الجنَّةِ.
The third section: al-sami'iyyat (things heard/revealed). And it is obligatory to believe in the existence of al-hur (the houris), plural of haura', and al-hawar is: extreme whiteness of the eye with extreme blackness of it, and they are the women of Paradise, and they are described as 'in (wide-eyed) because of the width of their eyes. And al-wildan (the youths): meaning the boys, and they are in the form of the boys of this world, and they are the servants of the people of Paradise. And it is said that they are the children of the disbelievers who die before puberty, for it has been related that they are the servants of the people of Paradise.
Source pages p. 158

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal statement on the sam'iyyat (revealed matters). Dardir first mentions the section heading, then states the obligation to believe in the Hoor (houris). He defines 'hawar' as extreme whiteness of the eye with intense blackness, and explains that they are the women of Paradise, described as 'in (wide-eyed). Then he discusses al-wildan (youths), who are like boys of this world and serve the people of Paradise. He also mentions an opinion that they are the children of disbelievers who died before puberty, based on a report that they are servants. The passage presents these as matters of belief to be accepted.

Key Terms
الحور
الحوَرُ
العِينِ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Hoor are metaphorical or symbolic beings.
Correction: Dardir presents them as real beings with specific, literal physical descriptions that must be believed.

Checkpoint
According to Dardir, what is the characteristic of the Hoor (houris)?
A) They have extremely white eyes
B) They have wide eyes with extreme whiteness and blackness
C) They are the same as the Wildan
D) They are children of disbelievers

Key Takeaway
Belief in the Hoor is obligatory; they are described with wide eyes having extreme whiteness and blackness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you knew for certain that the Hoor of Paradise are real and waiting for those who strive, what would you change about your actions starting today?
?
Do you find yourself more drawn to the fleeting beauties of this world or the eternal, perfect beauty promised in Paradise? What is one concrete step you can take this week to realign your desires?

The Hierarchical Ranking of the Companions
The author enumerates the ranking of the Companions and successors after the Prophet.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the specific ranking of the Companions and the early generations as established by Ahl al-Sunnah.

Core Idea
The Companions are ranked by merit, with the four rightly guided caliphs at the top.

This lesson presents the traditional hierarchy of the Companions and the generations that followed. Understanding this ranking is essential for respecting the virtues of each group and avoiding innovation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage listing the groups. Notice the order: 'Umar, 'Uthman, 'Ali, then the rest of the ten, etc.
The passage may have OCR issues: 'نَعُمَرُ' likely should be 'فَعُمَرُ'.
2
Identify each group
List the groups mentioned: the four caliphs, the remaining ten, the people of Badr, the people of the Pledge of Ridwan, the rest of the Companions, the Followers, and the Followers of the Followers.
3
Reflect on the significance
Why is this order important? It establishes a hierarchy that prevents disputing and elevates the status of each group.
Respecting this order is part of Ahl al-Sunnah's creed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نَعُمَرُ [؟]، فَعُثمانُ، فعلي، فبقيَّةُ العشَرةِ، فبقيَّةُ البدريين، فأهلُ بَيعَةِ الرّضوانِ، فقيّةُ [؟] الصحابة، فالتابعون فتابعو التابعين. ويجب الإمساك عما وقَعَ بَينَ الصحابةِ مِنَ النزاع (٢). (۲) لا يجوز الطعن في الصحابة، ويجب تأويل التشاجر الذي كان بينهم، وانتقاصهم زندقة، وجاء عن الإمام أحمد: من انتقص واحدا منهم وجب تأديبه أو حبسه حتى يموت أو يرجع، وقال مالك: إنما أراد هؤلاء القدح في النبي ، فلما لم يمكنهم ذلك قدحوا في أصحابه حتى يقال: رجل سوء ولو كان صالحا لكان أصحابه صالحين، وقال أحمد: إذا رأيت أحدا يذكرهم بسوء فاتهمه على الإسلام، وقال مالك : بلغني أن النصارى كانوا إذا رأوا الصحابة الذين فتحوا الشام يقولون: والله لهؤلاء خير من الحواريين.
Then 'Umar [؟], then 'Uthman, then 'Ali, then the rest of the ten, then the rest of the people of Badr, then the people of the Pledge of Ridwan, then the rest of the Companions [؟], then the Followers, then the Followers of the Followers. It is obligatory to refrain from [discussing] what occurred among the Companions of conflict (2). (2) It is not permissible to slander the Companions, and it is obligatory to interpret the quarrels that occurred among them [favorably], and belittling them is heresy. It is reported from Imam Ahmad: Whoever belittles one of them must be disciplined or imprisoned until he dies or repents. Malik said: These people only intended to discredit the Prophet, and when they could not do that, they discredited his Companions so that it could be said: He is a bad man, and if he were righteous, his Companions would be righteous. Ahmad said: If you see anyone mentioning them ill, suspect him of [being against] Islam. Malik said: It reached me that the Christians, when they saw the Companions who conquered Syria, would say: By God, these are better than the disciples.
Source pages p. 158

Commentary
This passage defines the ranking of the Companions after the Prophet and then gives a strong ruling on the obligation to respect them. The author lists the best after the Prophet: first the four rightly guided caliphs, then the remaining ten (the ten promised Paradise), then the people of Badr, then the people of the Pledge of Ridwan, then the rest of the Companions, then the Followers, then the Followers of the Followers. Then he states the obligation to refrain from discussing the conflicts that occurred among them. The footnote expands: slandering them is prohibited, and their disputes must be interpreted favorably. Belittling them is heresy. He cites Ahmad's severe penalty and Malik's reasoning that attacking the Companions is indirect attack on the Prophet.

Key Terms
الصحابة
البدريون
بيعة الرضوان
التابعون

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe that 'Ali is superior to Abu Bakr and 'Umar in rank.
Correction: The Ahl al-Sunnah consensus, as indicated by this passage, places 'Umar and 'Uthman above 'Ali in rank, following Abu Bakr.

Checkpoint
In the ranking given, who comes immediately after 'Uthman?
A) Abu Bakr
B) 'Umar
C) 'Ali
D) The rest of the ten

Key Takeaway
The Companions and early generations have a divinely ordained hierarchy based on virtue, which must be respected.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read about the ranking of the Companions, do you find any hidden resentment in your heart toward the order in which Abu Bakr and 'Umar are placed before 'Ali? If so, what is the source of that feeling, and how can you align your heart with the truth taught in this lesson?
?
This passage teaches that virtue among the early generations is not equal but hierarchical. How does this challenge your modern assumption that all people are equal in status? What does it mean for you to submit to Allah's judgment in ranking people by piety rather than by your own preferences?
?
If you were to honestly evaluate your own respect for the Companions, do you truly honor each group according to their rank, or do you find yourself elevating some (like 'Ali or the people of Badr) while neglecting others? What concrete action will you take this week to show proper veneration for all of them?

The Obligation to Refrain from Disputing the Companions
The author states the ruling on refraining from disputing the Companions and quotes scholars on the prohibition of slandering them.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the severe prohibition on slandering the Companions and the obligation to interpret their conflicts favorably.

Core Idea
Attacking the Companions is an attack on the Prophet himself.

This lesson focuses on the ruling regarding the disputes among the Companions. The scholars emphasize that we must respect their honor, remain silent about their conflicts, and interpret any disagreement in the best possible light, as belittling them is a sign of heresy.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and footnote
Read the ruling and the reports from Imam Ahmad and Imam Malik.
The footnote is part of the original text.
2
Understand the obligation
The passage states it is obligatory (يجب) to refrain from discussing what occurred among the Companions.
3
Analyze the proof from Malik
Malik reasoned that attacking the Companions is an indirect attack on the Prophet himself.
4
Reflect on the severity
Ahmad prescribed severe punishment for those who belittle a Companion, indicating the gravity of the sin.

Belief in the Maidens and Youths of Paradise
Definition of hur and wildan and the obligation of belief.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meanings of al-hur and al-wildan in Paradise and the obligation to believe in them.

Core Idea
Paradise has two distinct groups: wide-eyed maidens and eternal youths who serve the believers.

Sanusi explains two beloved features of Paradise: the hur and the wildan. These are not mere metaphors but real creations of Allah. In this passage, he defines them linguistically and theologically, establishing that belief in them is part of faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Note the linguistic terms and the structure.
The text has a minor corruption marker [؟]; the meaning is still clear from context.
2
Understand al-hur
Focus on the definition of al-hur: it is the plural of hawra', describing intense whiteness and blackness of the eye. They are the women of Paradise, described as wide-eyed.
3
Understand al-wildan
Al-wildan are youths in the form of the youths of this world. They serve the people of Paradise. There is also an opinion that they are the children of disbelievers who died before puberty.
4
Reflect on obligation
The passage begins with 'it is obligatory to believe'. Reflect on why these details matter for faith and how they relate to the unseen realities of Paradise.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإيمان (و) يجب الإيمان بوجودِ (الحور) جمع حوراء»، والحوَرُ: شِدَّةُ بياض العين مع بالحور [؟] يدة سوادها، وهُنَّ نساءُ الجَنَّةِ، وَوُصِفْنَ بِالعِينِ لانساعِ أَعْيُنِهِنَّ. (والولدان) أي: الغلمان، وهم على صورةِ عِلمانِ الدُّنيا، وهم خَدَمةُ أهل الجنّة. وقيل: إنهم أولادُ الكُفَّارِ الذين يموتون قبل البلوغ، فإنه ورَدَ أَنهم حَدَمةُ أَهْلَ الجنَّةِ.
Faith (and) it is obligatory to believe in the existence of al-hur (the maidens of Paradise), the plural of hawra'. Al-hawar is extreme whiteness of the eye with [؟] blackness. They are the women of Paradise, and they are described as wide-eyed because of the width of their eyes. (And al-wildan) meaning the youths. They are in the form of the youths of this world, and they are the servants of the people of Paradise. It is said: They are the children of the disbelievers who die before puberty, for it has been reported that they are the servants of the people of Paradise.
Source pages p. 158

Commentary
This passage defines two elements of Paradise: the hur and the wildan. It first defines al-hur linguistically as hawra' meaning intense whiteness of the eye contrasted with intense blackness, then clarifies they are the women of Paradise, described as wide-eyed. Then it defines al-wildan as young male servants, like the youths of this world. It mentions a secondary opinion that these youths are the children of disbelievers who died before puberty. The passage establishes that belief in these is obligatory.

Key Terms
الحور
الولدان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-wildan are ordinary human children who died before puberty and are simply playing in Paradise.
Correction: The passage states that al-wildan are created beings in the form of youths, appointed as servants of the people of Paradise. The opinion that they are children of disbelievers does not make them ordinary children; they have a specific servitor role.

Checkpoint
What is the primary meaning of al-hur?
A) Young boys
B) Women of Paradise with wide eyes
C) Servants
D) Children of believers

Key Takeaway
Belief in the hur and wildan is obligatory; they are real creations of Allah in Paradise with specific descriptions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that Paradise will contain beings like the hur and wildan, or does your mind treat them as mere symbols? What change would it make in your daily life if you genuinely felt their reality? This week, commit to visualizing one description of Paradise each morning to strengthen your conviction.
?
The passage says it is obligatory to believe in the existence of these invisible beings. Is your belief in them active and alive, or just a passive acknowledgment? What can you do today to move from knowing about them to longing for them?
?
When you read that the wildan may be the children of disbelievers serving believers, does it cause any discomfort? How does this challenge your understanding of Allah's justice and mercy? Take time to reflect on the wisdom behind such a decree and submit wholeheartedly to it.

Belief in the Saints and Their Miracles
Definition of wali, nature of sainthood, and obligation to believe in karamat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of a saint (wali), the nature of sainthood as a divine gift, and the distinction between saintly miracles (karamat) and prophetic miracles.

Core Idea
Saints are not sinless but divinely preserved; their miracles confirm righteousness without claiming prophethood.

This passage from Imam Dardir's Sharh al-Kharidah establishes the essential beliefs regarding Allah's saints. It defines who they are, clarifies that sainthood is a gift not earned, and explains the concept of karamat. The text also addresses a common misunderstanding about the sinlessness of saints.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition of a wali
Read the definition carefully: a wali is one who fulfills the rights of Allah and people, knows Allah, and consistently obeys while avoiding sin.
Note the phrase 'according to ability'—it acknowledges human limitation.
2
Learn about sainthood (al-wilaya)
The footnote explains that sainthood, like prophethood, is a divine favor, not gained by effort. Unlike prophethood, it is not disbelief to say it can be acquired.
This distinction is important in Sunni theology.
3
Understand the protection of saints
Saints are not sinless (ma'sum) but are preserved (mahfuzun)—if they sin, Allah guides them to repentance.
This answers the misconception that saints are perfect.
4
Define and believe in karamat
A karama is an extraordinary event at the hand of a righteous person, not accompanied by a claim to prophethood. Belief in karamat is obligatory based on Quran, Sunnah, and consensus.
This distinguishes them from prophetic miracles (mu'jizat).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يجب الإيمان بـ (الأوليا) جمعُ ولي(۳)، وهو: القائم بحقوق الله تعالى وحقوقِ العباد حسب الإمكان، وهو معنى قولِ مَنْ قال: هو العارف بالله تعالى وصفاته حسب الإمكان، المواظب على الطاعات، المجتَنِبُ للمُخالفات، المعرِضُ عن الانهماك في اللذات والشهوات (٤). وعبد الرحمن بن عوف وسعد بن أبي وقاص وسعيد بن زيد، وتخصيص هؤلاء العشرة بأنهم أن المبشرين أكثر منهم الحسن والحسين وفاطمة عليهم السلام- لأن العشرة جمعوا في حديث واحد، والأفضل بعد العشرة أهل بدر ثم أحد ثم أهل بيعة الرضوان. المبشرون بالجنة -مع (1) أسقط الشارح أهل أحد، ورتبتهم تلي رتبة البدريين في الأفضلية. (۲) لا يجوز الطعن في الصحابة، ويجب تأويل التشاجر الذي كان بينهم، وانتقاصهم زندقة، وجاء عن الإمام أحمد: من انتقص واحدا منهم وجب تأديبه أو حبسه حتى يموت أو يرجع، وقال مالك: إنما أراد هؤلاء القدح في النبي ، فلما لم يمكنهم ذلك قدحوا في أصحابه حتى يقال: رجل سوء ولو كان صالحا لكان أصحابه صالحين، وقال أحمد: إذا رأيت أحدا يذكرهم بسوء فاتهمه على الإسلام، وقال مالك : بلغني أن النصارى كانوا إذا رأوا الصحابة الذين فتحوا الشام يقولون: والله لهؤلاء خير من الحواريين. (۳) الولاية كالنبوة، ليستا تنالان ،بالكسب فهي فضل منه سبحانه، وهذا هو الظاهر، ولا يكفر من جوز اكتسابها بخلاف النبوة. (4) الأولياء محفوظون ، بمعنى أنهم إذا أذنبوا وفقهم الله للتوبة، لا معصومون، ولذلك لا يمتنع وقوع الذنب منهم. ويجب اعتقاد كراماتهم، والكرامة : أمر خارق للعادة يظهرُ على يد عبد الصلاح، غَيْرُ مقرون بدَعْوى النُّبوّة. كُلُّ ذلك ورَدَ به الكِتابُ والسُّنّة وأجمعت عليه الأمةُ قبلَ ظُهور المخالفين، وكُلُّ ما كانَ كذلك فالإيمان به واجبٌ.
It is obligatory to believe in al-awliya' (the saints), the plural of wali (3), and he is the one who fulfills the rights of Allah and the rights of the servants according to ability, and that is the meaning of whoever said: he is the knower of Allah and His attributes according to ability, constant in obedience, avoiding disobedience, turning away from indulgence in pleasures and desires (4). And Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf, Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas, and Sa'id ibn Zayd, and specifying these ten as being the ten who were given glad tidings, but more than them are al-Hasan, al-Husayn, and Fatima (peace be upon them) — because the ten were gathered in one hadith, and after the ten the most virtuous are the people of Badr, then Uhud, then the people of the Pledge of Ridwan. The ones given glad tidings of Paradise — with (1) the commentator omitted the people of Uhud, and their rank follows the rank of the people of Badr in superiority. (2) It is not permissible to defame the Companions, and it is obligatory to interpret the quarrels that occurred among them [favorably], and belittling them is heresy, and it is reported from Imam Ahmad: Whoever belittles one of them must be disciplined or imprisoned until he dies or repents, and Malik said: These people only intended to discredit the Prophet, and when they could not do that, they discredited his Companions so that it could be said: He is a bad man, and if he were righteous, his Companions would be righteous, and Ahmad said: If you see anyone mentioning them ill, suspect him of [being against] Islam, and Malik said: It reached me that the Christians, when they saw the Companions who conquered Syria, would say: By God, these are better than the disciples. (3) Sainthood is like prophethood, they are not attained by effort, rather they are a favor from Him (Glory be to Him), and this is what is apparent, and one who permits acquiring it is not a disbeliever, unlike prophethood. (4) The saints are preserved, meaning that if they sin, Allah grants them repentance; they are not sinless, and therefore the occurrence of sin from them is not impossible. And it is obligatory to believe in their miracles (karamat), and the miracle is an extraordinary event that appears at the hand of a righteous servant, not accompanied by a claim of prophethood. All of this has been reported in the Book and the Sunnah, and the Umma has agreed upon it before the appearance of the opponents, and everything that is like that, belief in it is obligatory.
Source pages p. 158

Commentary
This passage is a mix of two topics. The primary topic is belief in the saints and their miracles. The passage begins by defining a wali as one who fulfills rights and is a knower of Allah, constant in acts of worship, avoiding sins. Then it includes a section on the ten Companions, which is a separate topic about the Companions. The footnote (3) discusses that sainthood is not acquired by effort but is a gift from Allah, unlike prophethood which cannot be acquired. Footnote (4) clarifies that saints are not sinless but are protected in that they are guided to repentance. Then it returns to the main topic: belief in their miracles (karamat). A miracle is defined as an extraordinary event at the hand of a righteous person, not accompanied by a claim to prophethood. The passage concludes that all this is based on Quran and Sunnah and early consensus, so belief is obligatory.

Key Terms
الأولياء
الولاية
الكرامة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think saints are sinless like prophets.
Correction: The passage clarifies that saints are not sinless but are preserved (محفوظون) and may sin and then repent.

Checkpoint
What distinguishes a saintly miracle (karama) from a prophetic miracle (mu'jiza)?
A) Karamat are not extraordinary
B) Karamat are not accompanied by a claim to prophethood
C) Karamat only occur for prophets
D) Karamat are not from Allah

Key Takeaway
Saints are righteous servants preserved by Allah, and their miracles are real and obligatory to believe in, but they are not sinless or prophets.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that the miracles of saints are real and can affect your life today, or do you secretly dismiss them as exaggerated stories? What would change if you took them seriously?
?
If sainthood is a divine gift and not earned, does that make you feel relieved or uneasy? Do you rely on your own efforts for closeness to Allah, or do you humbly ask for His gift of wilayah?
?
When you hear of a righteous person committing a sin, do you judge them as a hypocrite, or do you remember that saints are preserved, not sinless, and that Allah facilitates their repentance? How does this lesson change how you view the flaws of pious Muslims?

The Virtue and Rights of the Companions
Enumeration of the ten Companions and rulings on their virtue and defamation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the special status of the ten Companions given glad tidings of Paradise, the hierarchy of virtue among the Companions, and the ruling on those who defame them.

Core Idea
Defaming any Companion is heresy; the Companions must be respected and their conflicts interpreted favorably.

This segment from the same text addresses the Companions of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him). It lists some of the ten promised Paradise, notes the superior virtue of the people of Badr and Uhud, and then provides strong warnings against speaking ill of any Companion. The great Imams Ahmad and Malik have severe rulings on this matter.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ten Companions
The text mentions Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf, Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas, Sa'id ibn Zayd, and notes that al-Hasan, al-Husayn, and Fatima are also included though not part of the ten. The ten are those gathered in one hadith.
The full list of ten is well-known: Abu Bakr, Umar, Uthman, Ali, Talha, Zubayr, Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf, Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas, Sa'id ibn Zayd, and Abu Ubayda.
2
Understand the hierarchy of virtue
After the ten, the most virtuous are the people of Badr, then the people of Uhud, then the people of the Pledge of Ridwan.
The commentator omitted the people of Uhud in some versions.
3
Learn the ruling on defaming Companions
It is not permissible to defame any Companion. The quarrels among them must be interpreted favorably. Belittling them is considered heresy (zandaqa). Imam Ahmad says such a person must be disciplined or imprisoned until death or repentance. Imam Malik adds that attacking the Companions is an indirect attack on the Prophet.
This shows the high regard for the Companions in Sunni Islam.

?

?

Belief in Everything the Prophet Brought
The author states the obligation to believe in all that the Prophet brought, as it has become necessary knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that it is obligatory to believe in everything widely reported from the Prophet, as it has reached the level of necessary knowledge.

Core Idea
The Prophet's well-known reports are as certain as necessary knowledge.

This passage establishes a foundational principle in Sunni theology: everything authentically reported from the Prophet (peace be upon him) must be believed, especially when it has become so widespread that no one can plausibly deny it. The author explains why such reports are treated like necessary knowledge and provides concrete examples, including the famous account of the Mi'raj (ascension).

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation side by side to get a feel for the author's language and argument.
The passage interweaves the poetic line with commentary.
2
Identify the principle
Find the core statement: 'everything that came from the bearer of good news... has become like the necessary.' Understand that this is an obligation to believe.
The phrase 'صار كالضروري' is key – it means it has become like self-evident truth.
3
Understand 'necessary knowledge'
The author says these matters have become so widely known among elite and commoners that they are like necessary knowledge (daruri), impossible to deny.
This differs from logical necessity; it's widespread acceptance.
4
Examine the examples
The passage lists obligatory acts, prohibitions, permissibilities, and the Mi'raj. Notice that the Mi'raj is included as a matter of belief.
The Mi'raj is described in detail, showing it is a central example.
5
Reflect on the lesson
Ask yourself: why is it important to believe in these well-known reports? How does this principle affect your understanding of Islamic theology?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٥٧ - وكُلّ ما جاءَ عن البشير * مِنْ كُلِّ حُكْم صارَ كَالضَّروري (و) كذا يجب الإيمان بـ كُلِّ ما جاءَ) أي: رُويَ ونُقِلَ (عنْ) أَيْ: عن النبي بكل ما جاء عن البشير (البشير) أي: المبشِّرِ لمن أوفى بالعُهود بأنه محمود العاقبة . مِنْ كُلِّ حُكْم) بيان لكُلِّ ما جاءَ (صارَ) في الاشتهار بَينَ الخاصة والعامة (ك) الأمر (الضروري) الذي لا يخفى على أحَدٍ. وهذا مِنْ عطْفِ العام على الخاص لشموله ما تَقَدَّمَ مِنَ الحِسابِ وما عُطِفَ عليه وغيره: - كوجوب شَهادةِ أنْ لا إلهَ إلا الله وأنَّ مُحمّدًا رسولُ اللهِ، وإقام الصلاة، وإيتاء الزَّكاةِ، وصَومِ رمَضانَ ، وحَجٌ بَيتِ الله الحرام، وحُرمةِ الزِّنا والخمْرِ والرِّبا، وحِل النكاح والبيع، ونحو ذلك. - وكالمعراج بجَسَدِه الشريف صلى الله عليه وسلم يقظة، وهو العُروجُ إلى السماء معَ جبريل العَلَيْكُرُ [؟] بلا بُراق، بعد الإسراء ليلا مِنَ المسجد الحرام إلى المسجد الأقصى راكبًا للبراق، وهو دابّة أبيضُ طويلٌ، فَوقَ الحِمارِ، ودونَ البَغَلِ، يَضَعُ حافِرَه عِندَ مُنتهى طرفه . والمراد بالمعراج ما يعم الإسراء، وقصته مشهورة.
57. And everything that came from the bearer of good news, of every ruling, has become like the necessary. (And) likewise, it is obligatory to believe in everything that came (i.e., was narrated and transmitted) from (i.e., from the Prophet), with everything that came from the bearer of good news (al-bashir) i.e., the one who gives glad tidings to those who fulfill the covenants that their end is praiseworthy. 'Of every ruling' is an explanation of 'everything that came'. 'Has become' in widespreadness among the elite and commoners like the necessary matter (al-daruri) which is not hidden from anyone. And this is joining the general to the particular to include what has preceded of the reckoning and what is conjoined with it and other things: such as the obligation of the testimony that there is no god but Allah and that Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah, establishing prayer, giving zakat, fasting Ramadan, pilgrimage to the Sacred House of Allah, the prohibition of adultery, wine, usury, the permissibility of marriage and sale, and the like. And such as the Mi'raj with his noble body (peace be upon him) while awake, which is the ascension to the heavens with Jibril (peace be upon him) [؟] without a Buraq, after the Isra' by night from the Sacred Mosque to the Aqsa Mosque riding the Buraq, which is a white animal, long, larger than a donkey and smaller than a mule, placing its hoof at the limit of its sight. And what is meant by the Mi'raj encompasses the Isra', and its story is well-known.
Source pages p. 159

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the line of poetry. It establishes a general principle: belief in everything that the Prophet brought is obligatory, and such well-known matters are like necessary knowledge (daruri) — i.e., so widely known that no one can deny them. It then gives examples: the five pillars, prohibitions, and permissibilities. It also includes the Mi'raj (ascension) as a specific example. The Mi'raj is described as bodily, in wakefulness, with Jibril, without Buraq for the ascension itself (though Buraq was used for the Isra' travel). The passage emphasizes that these are matters of consensus.

Key Terms
البشير
الضروري
المعراج
الإسراء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why are the rulings from the Prophet considered like necessary knowledge?
A) They are logically necessary
B) They are so widespread and well-known
C) They are from the Quran
D) They are the result of Ijma

Key Takeaway
It is obligatory to believe in everything widely reported from the Prophet, including the Mi'raj, as such reports have become like self-evident truths due to their widespread acceptance.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly accept every report from the Prophet, including those that challenge your rational mind, or do you find yourself hesitating with some? What does that hesitation reveal about your iman?
?
The author says the Prophet's reports have become 'like necessary knowledge' due to widespread transmission. But do you live as if that knowledge is as certain as the sun rising? Give a specific example from your life where you acted on a prophetic teaching with that level of certainty.
?
When you hear the story of the Mi'raj, do you accept it as literally true, or does your heart seek to reinterpret it? How does your answer affect your relationship with the Prophet?

The Arrival of Munkar and Nakir and the Believer's Response
Dardeer describes the arrival of Munkar and Nakir, the questions, and the believer's answer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the events of the grave questioning, including the description of the angels, the universal nature of the questioning, and the believer's correct response and reward.

Core Idea
The grave questioning is a reality for every soul; the believer is honored with a vision of Paradise.

Imam Dardeer begins by establishing the reality of the grave questioning, describing the two angels Munkar and Nakir who come to every deceased person regardless of their faith. This passage outlines the process from the moment the angels arrive to the moment the believer is shown his seat in Paradise. It affirms that this questioning is a universal trial that awaits all.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once and then the translation. Let the sequence of events sink in before analyzing.
Notice the mentions of the return of the soul; these are elaborated later.
2
Describe the angels and the timing
Identify the physical description of Munkar and Nakir and the precise time they come to the deceased.
They come after burial when people depart.
3
List the three questions
Write down the three questions asked by the angels as they appear in the text.
4
Observe the believer's answer and reward
Note what the believer says and how the angels respond by showing him his seat in Paradise.
This shows the immediate reward of correct faith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكسؤال الملكين منكر ونكير، وهما ملكان أسْوَدانِ أَزْرَقانِ، أَيْ: أَعيُنُهما، يأتيان للميت، مؤمنا كان أو كافِرًا أو مُنافِقًا)، بعد تمام الدفن في القبر الذي يستَقِرُّ فيه دائما، وعند انصراف الناسِ فيُقعدانه، ويُعيدُ الله فيه الروحَ بِتَمامِه (۲)، وقيل: في نِصفه(۳)، ويسألانه «مَنْ رَبُّكَ وما دينُكَ، وما تقولُ في الرَّجُلِ الذي بُعِثَ فيكم ؟ (4) فيقول المؤمِنُ : ربي الله ، وديني الإسلام، والرجُلُ المبعوث فينا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ، فيقولان له «انظُرْ مَقْعَدَكَ مِنَ النَّارِ قَدْ أَبدَلَكَ الله به مقعدًا في الجنّة» فيراهما جميعًا. وأمّا المنافقُ أو الكافر (ه) فيقول : لا أدري ، فيقولان له «لا دريت ولا تليتَ»، ويُضَرَبُ بمطراق من حديد في يد أحدهما، فيصيحُ صَيحةً يسمَعُها مَنْ يليهِ غَيْرَ الثقلين. ويتَرفَقانِ بالمؤمن، وينهران الكافر والمنافق. ويسألان كُلَّ أحد بلسانه على الصحيح )، ولو تمزّقت أعضاؤه أو أكلته السِّباعُ أو حُرِقَ وسُحِقَ وذُريَ في الهواءِ، إذ لا يبعدُ أنْ يخلُقَ اللهُ تعالى الحياة فيه. (۱) هذا هو الصحيح خلافا لقول ابن عبد البر والسيوطي: لا يسأل الكافر. [صاوي، ص ٦٨] (۲) هذا هو قول الجمهور لظاهر الأحاديث المتواترة، ولذا قال السيوطي: وكله يحيا لدى الجمهور * لا جزءه لظاهر المأثور [صاوي، ص ٦١] (۳) تعاد الروح إلى البدن وقت السؤال، وقال ابن حجر والظاهر أنها في نصف الميت الأعلى فيسأل البدن وفيه الروح. وهذه الحياة لا تنفي اسم الميت عنه، بل هي أمر متوسط بين الموت والحياة كتوسط النوم بينهما. (٤) السؤال في القبر على العقائد فقط، وفي رواية: يسأل ومن أبوك ؟ وما قبلتك ؟ (٥) جزم ابن عبد البر في تمهيده بأن الكافر لا يسأل، وإنما يسأل المؤمن والمنافق لانتسابه إلى الإسلام في الظاهر . (1) يقول الباجوري: ويسألان كل أحد بلسانه على الصحيح، خلافا لمن قال بالسرياني»، ولذلك قال بعضهم ومن عجيب ما ترى العينان * أن سؤال القبر بالسرياني [تحفة المريد ١٠٤] أفتى بهذا شيخنا البلقيني * ولم أره لغيره بعيني
And also the questioning of the two angels Munkar and Nakir. They are two black, blue-eyed angels, meaning their eyes, who come to the deceased, whether believer, disbeliever, or hypocrite, after the completion of burial in the grave where he will remain permanently. And when the people depart, they make him sit up, and Allah returns the soul to him completely (according to the majority) or it is said in half of him. And they ask him: 'Who is your Lord, and what is your religion, and what do you say about the man who was sent among you?' So the believer says: 'My Lord is Allah, my religion is Islam, and the man sent among us is the Messenger of Allah,' peace be upon him. So they say to him: 'Look at your seat from the Fire; Allah has replaced it for you with a seat in Paradise.' So he sees both of them. As for the hypocrite or the disbeliever, he says: 'I do not know.' So they say to him: 'You do not know and you did not learn?' And he is struck with an iron hammer in the hand of one of them, and he cries out a cry that is heard by those near him except for the two weighty classes (jinn and humans). And they are gentle with the believer, and they scold the disbeliever and hypocrite. And they question everyone in his own tongue according to the correct view. And even if his limbs are torn apart, or beasts eat him, or he is burned, ground, and scattered in the air, it is not impossible for Allah Almighty to create life in him. (1) This is the correct view contrary to the saying of Ibn 'Abd al-Barr and al-Suyuti that the disbeliever is not questioned. (2) This is the view of the majority due to the apparent meaning of the mutawatir narrations, and therefore al-Suyuti said: 'All of him lives according to the majority, not part of him, due to the apparent transmitted report.' (3) The soul is returned to the body at the time of questioning, and Ibn Hajar said that apparently it is in the upper half of the deceased, so the body is questioned with the soul in it. And this life does not negate the name 'dead' from him; rather it is a matter intermediate between death and life, like the intermediate state of sleep between the two. (4) The questioning in the grave is only about creed, and in one narration: he is asked: 'Who is your father? and what is your direction of prayer?' (5) Ibn 'Abd al-Barr asserted in his Tamhid that the disbeliever is not questioned, and that only the believer and the hypocrite are questioned because of their outward affiliation to Islam. (1) Al-Bajuri says: 'And they question everyone in his own tongue according to the correct view, contrary to those who say it is in Syriac,' and therefore some said: 'And among the wondrous things that the eyes see is that the questioning in the grave is in Syriac, our shaykh al-Bulqini gave a fatwa on this, and I have not seen it from anyone else by my eyes.'
Source pages p. 160

Commentary
This passage discusses the questioning in the grave by the two angels Munkar and Nakir. The author begins by stating that this is among the matters that came from the Prophet. He describes the angels as black and blue-eyed, and they come to every deceased person—believer, disbeliever, or hypocrite—after the burial is complete. The deceased is made to sit up, and Allah returns his soul completely (according to the majority) or partially. Then the angels ask three questions: 'Who is your Lord? What is your religion? What do you say about the man who was sent among you?' The believer answers correctly, and is shown his seat in Paradise. The hypocrite or disbeliever says 'I do not know' and is struck with a hammer and cries out. The author also notes that the angels are gentle with the believer but harsh with the other. He affirms that the questioning is in the person's own language, and that even if the body is destroyed, Allah can recreate life in it. The passage includes several editorial notes: the first clarifies that the correct view is that the disbeliever is also questioned, contrary to Ibn 'Abd al-Barr and al-Suyuti. The second note discusses the return of the soul completely versus partially, quoting the majority view and al-Suyuti's verse. The third note explains the intermediate state of life during questioning. The fourth note restricts the questioning to creedal matters. The fifth note repeats the ruling about the disbeliever. The final note rejects the view that the questioning is in Syriac, affirming it is in the person's own language.

Key Terms
منكر ونكير
سؤال القبر
إعادة الروح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the grave questioning is only for believers or only for Muslims.
Correction: The passage explicitly states it is for every deceased: 'believer, disbeliever, or hypocrite.'

Checkpoint
What does the believer say when asked about the man sent among them?
A) 'I do not know'
B) 'He is the Messenger of Allah'
C) 'He is a righteous man'
D) 'He is a prophet of the Jews'

Key Takeaway
The grave questioning is a real event for every soul, and the believer's correct confession brings the reward of Paradise.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were made to sit in your grave right now and asked 'Who is your Lord?', would your answer come from deep certainty or mere habit? What in your daily life proves that Allah is truly your Lord?
?
You have just learned that every soul—believer, disbeliever, and hypocrite—will be questioned. Does this make you examine your own faith more seriously, or do you assume you are safe? What would it take for you to truly prepare for that moment?
?
The believer is shown his seat in Paradise while still in the grave. If you could see your final destination tonight, would it bring you joy or terror? What one change can you make before sunrise to secure a better seat?

The Fate of the Hypocrite and Disbeliever in the Grave
Dardeer describes the response and punishment of the hypocrite and disbeliever.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the hypocrite and disbeliever respond to the grave questioning and the punishment they receive.

Core Idea
The hypocrite and disbeliever are punished with ignorance and a blow from an iron hammer.

After describing the believer's success, Dardeer turns to the fate of those who fail the test. The hypocrite or disbeliever cannot answer the questions and is struck with a terrible hammer, causing a cry heard by all except humans and jinn. This passage highlights the severe consequences of disbelief and hypocrisy.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage describing the hypocrite and disbeliever
Pay attention to their answer: 'I do not know.' This is a stark contrast to the believer's reply.
2
Note the angels' response
Observe how the angels rebuke them with 'You do not know and you did not learn?' and then strike them.
The rebuke implies they had the means to know but rejected the truth.
3
Consider the contrast in treatment
The passage states that the angels are gentle with the believer but scold the hypocrite and disbeliever.

Theological Disputes on the Grave Questioning
Dardeer presents scholarly clarifications on the return of the soul, language, and universality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scholarly positions on whether the soul returns completely or partially, the language of the questioning, and the power of Allah to reconstitute the body.

Core Idea
The grave questioning involves a special life, and the soul returns to the body in a way that does not contradict death.

The passage concludes with several important theological clarifications. The first is that the correct view is that all people are questioned, including disbelievers. Then there is a discussion of whether the soul returns to the entire body or just part of it, with the majority favoring the entire body. Finally, the issue of the language of questioning is settled: it is in the person's own tongue, not Syriac. These points show that kalam engages in reasoned elaboration of transmitted texts.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage containing the scholarly notes
This part is a series of clarifications. Read them one by one.
The notes are numbered in the text.
2
Understand the majority view on the return of the soul
Note that the majority say the soul returns to the entire body, not just part.
Al-Suyuti's verse is quoted: 'All of him lives...'
3
Understand the language of questioning
The correct view is that the questioning is in the person's own language, contra the Syriac claim.
Al-Bajuri is cited affirming this.
4
Reflect on Allah's power
Even if the body is destroyed, Allah can recreate life in it for the questioning.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And also the questioning of the two angels Munkar and Nakir. They are two black, blue-eyed angels, meaning their eyes, who come to the deceased, whether believer, disbeliever, or hypocrite, after the completion of burial in the grave where he will remain permanently. And when the people depart, they make him sit up, and Allah returns the soul to him completely (according to the majority) or it is said in half of him. As for the hypocrite or the disbeliever, he says: 'I do not know.' So they say to him: 'You do not know and you did not learn?' And he is struck with an iron hammer in the hand of one of them, and he cries out a cry that is heard by those near him except for the two weighty classes (jinn and humans). And they are gentle with the believer, and they scold the disbeliever and hypocrite. And they question everyone in his own tongue according to the correct view. And even if his limbs are torn apart, or beasts eat him, or he is burned, ground, and scattered in the air, it is not impossible for Allah Almighty to create life in him. (1) This is the correct view contrary to the saying of Ibn 'Abd al-Barr and al-Suyuti that the disbeliever is not questioned. (2) This is the view of the majority due to the apparent meaning of the mutawatir narrations, and therefore al-Suyuti said: 'All of him lives according to the majority, not part of him, due to the apparent transmitted report.' (3) The soul is returned to the body at the time of questioning, and Ibn Hajar said that apparently it is in the upper half of the deceased, so the body is questioned with the soul in it. And this life does not negate the name 'dead' from him; rather it is a matter intermediate between death and life, like the intermediate state of sleep between the two. (4) The questioning in the grave is only about creed, and in one narration: he is asked: 'Who is your father? and what is your direction of prayer?' (5) Ibn 'Abd al-Barr asserted in his Tamhid that the disbeliever is not questioned, and that only the believer and the hypocrite are questioned because of their outward affiliation to Islam. (1) Al-Bajuri says: 'And they question everyone in his own tongue according to the correct view, contrary to those who say it is in Syriac,' and therefore some said: 'And among the wondrous things that the eyes see is that the questioning in the grave is in Syriac, our shaykh al-Bulqini gave a fatwa on this, and I have not seen it from anyone else by my eyes.'
Source pages p. 160

Commentary
This passage discusses the questioning in the grave by the two angels Munkar and Nakir. The author begins by stating that this is among the matters that came from the Prophet. He describes the angels as black and blue-eyed, and they come to every deceased person—believer, disbeliever, or hypocrite—after the burial is complete. The deceased is made to sit up, and Allah returns his soul completely (according to the majority) or partially. Then the angels ask three questions: 'Who is your Lord? What is your religion? What do you say about the man who was sent among you?' The believer answers correctly, and is shown his seat in Paradise. The hypocrite or disbeliever says 'I do not know' and is struck with a hammer and cries out. The author also notes that the angels are gentle with the believer but harsh with the other. He affirms that the questioning is in the person's own language, and that even if the body is destroyed, Allah can recreate life in it. The passage includes several editorial notes: the first clarifies that the correct view is that the disbeliever is also questioned, contrary to Ibn 'Abd al-Barr and al-Suyuti. The second note discusses the return of the soul completely versus partially, quoting the majority view and al-Suyuti's verse. The third note explains the intermediate state of life during questioning. The fourth note restricts the questioning to creedal matters. The fifth note repeats the ruling about the disbeliever. The final note rejects the view that the questioning is in Syriac, affirming it is in the person's own language.

Key Terms
إعادة الروح
بلسان
سرياني

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some claim the questioning in the grave is in Syriac.
Correction: The passage asserts the correct view is that it is in the person's own tongue.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the language of the grave questioning?
A) Syriac
B) Hebrew
C) One's own tongue
D) Arabic

Key Takeaway
The grave questioning is universal, the soul returns to the body in a special intermediate life, and the questions are asked in each person's own language.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The questioning will be in your own tongue about your creed. If you were asked right now, 'Who is your Lord? What is your religion? Who is your Prophet?' would you answer with certainty? What doubt, if any, lingers in your heart that you must uproot today?
?
The passage says Allah can recreate life even if your body is scattered to the winds. Do you truly believe He has power over everything, including your own death? How does that belief affect the choices you make tonight?
?
The grave questioning is an intermediate life like sleep — you will be aware, awake, and accountable. If you were to die tonight, what single sin or neglect would you most regret? What will you do before this day ends to prepare for that moment?

The Two Angels Nakir and Munkir and the Questioning of the Believer
Describes the two angels and the questioning of the deceased.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic belief regarding the two angels of the grave, their appearance, the universal questioning of all deceased, and the reward of the believer for correct answers.

Core Idea
Every soul is questioned in the grave about its Lord, religion, and Prophet.

This lesson introduces a key revealed matter (sam'iyyat): the questioning in the grave by the two angels Munkar and Nakir. The author describes their appearance and the process after burial, emphasizing that this trial applies to every deceased person. You will see how the believer answers and what reward he receives.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the translation. Let the author's description of the angels and the questioning come through before you interpret.
Notice the descriptive details about the angels' appearance.
2
Notice the universality of the questioning
The text says the angels come to every deceased person: believer, disbeliever, or hypocrite. This is important because some mistakenly think only believers are questioned.
3
Identify the three questions
Find the three questions the angels ask: about the Lord, religion, and the Prophet. These are the fundamental beliefs of Islam.
These are the same questions every Muslim should know.
4
Understand the believer's response and reward
The believer answers correctly and is shown his seat in Paradise, which was replaced from a seat in the Fire. This shows the mercy of Allah.
The reward is both a visual and a promise.

The third section: The revealed matters (al-sam'iyyat). And like the questioning of the two angels Munkar and Nakir; they are two black, blue-eyed angels, i.e., their eyes are blue, who come to the deceased, whether he is a believer, a disbeliever, or a hypocrite, after the completion of burial in the grave where he settles permanently, and when the people depart, they sit him up. And God returns the soul to him in its entirety (2), and it is said: in its half (3). So they say to him: 'Look at your seat from the Fire; Allah has replaced it for you with a seat in Paradise.' So he sees both of them.

This passage begins the third section on revealed matters (al-sam'iyyat). It describes the two angels of the grave, Munkar and Nakir, who are black with blue eyes. They come to every deceased person after burial, sit them up, and God returns the soul. The questioning is about the three fundamental beliefs: Lord, religion, and the Prophet. The believer answers correctly and is shown his seat in Paradise replaced from the Fire.
