The Punishment of the Hypocrite and Disbeliever in the Grave
Describes the response and punishment of the hypocrite/disbeliever in the grave.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the specific response of the hypocrite or disbeliever during the grave questioning and the nature of their punishment as described in the source.

Core Idea
The hypocrite and disbeliever face a terrifying punishment: ignorance and a physical strike.

In this lesson, we examine a vivid description from the Islamic tradition about the fate of the hypocrite or disbeliever in the grave. The passage reveals not only their words but also the painful consequence they face. Let us read the Arabic text and its translation to grasp the severity of this moment.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text carefully. Notice the concise description of the hypocrite's response and the subsequent action by the angels.
The passage uses strong imagery: 'sledgehammer of iron' and a scream heard by all except humans and jinn.
2
Understand the translation
Read the literal translation. Identify the key elements: the hypocrite's words, the angels' rebuke, the strike, and the scream.
3
Analyze the details
Consider why the hypocrite says 'I do not know' and what the angels' response 'you did not know and you did not recite' implies about their disbelief.
This highlights the consequence of rejecting truth in life.
4
Reflect on the exception
The scream is heard by all except the 'thaqalayn' (humans and jinn). Why might this exception exist? It emphasizes the hidden nature of the punishment from living beings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأمّا المنافقُ أو الكافر (ه) فيقول : لا أدري ، فيقولان له «لا دريت ولا تليتَ»، ويُضَرَبُ بمطراق من حديد في يد أحدهما، فيصيحُ صَيحةً يسمَعُها مَنْ يليهِ غَيْرَ الثقلين.

Commentary
This passage explains what happens to the hypocrite or disbeliever during the questioning. He responds with ignorance, so the angels rebuke him and strike him with an iron hammer. The scream is so loud that all creatures nearby hear it except humans and jinn (the thaqalayn), indicating the severity of the punishment.

?

General Rules of the Grave Questioning
Discusses the scope of questioning, the return of the soul, and who is exempt.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scope of the grave questioning, including who is questioned, in what manner, and who is exempt.

Core Idea
The grave questioning applies to all accountable beings, but many are exempt by divine mercy.

Imam Dardeer now discusses the general rules of the grave questioning, covering its universal application, the variation in how it occurs, and the extensive list of those who are exempt. This passage clarifies that questioning is not limited to believers, yet many categories are spared from this trial.

Guided Path
1
Understand the universality
Read the first part: questioning happens to everyone, in their own language, even if the body is completely destroyed. Reflect on how God can recreate life for this purpose.
This shows the power of Allah in resurrection.
2
Note the variation in questioning
The passage explains that the manner and extent of questioning differ based on the person's state. Some are asked by both angels, some by one, and some are asked about part or all of their beliefs.
Al-Qurtubi's quote highlights this variation.
3
Learn the exemptions
Go through the list of those who are not questioned: prophets, angels, siddiqun, murabitun, martyrs, those who regularly recite Tabarak, those who recite al-Ikhlas on deathbed, those who die of stomach disease, plague victims, insane, and mentally deficient.
Also note that children are not questioned according to al-Suyuti.
4
Consider the jinn
The passage states that jinn are questioned because they are obligated (mukallaf). This shows the general rule applies to all rational beings.
5
Conclude with the trial
The questioning is identified as the 'trial of the grave' (fitnat al-qabr). This is the ultimate purpose of the questioning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويسألان كُلَّ أحد بلسانه على الصحيح )، ولو تمزّقت أعضاؤه أو أكلته السِّباعُ أو حُرِقَ وسُحِقَ وذُريَ في الهواءِ، إذ لا يبعدُ أنْ يخلُقَ اللهُ تعالى الحياة فيه.
وأحوال المسئولين مختلفةٌ: فمنهم مَنْ يسأله الملكان، ومنهم مَنْ يسأله أحدهما. قال القُرطبي: «اختَلَفتِ الأحاديثُ في كَيفيّةِ السؤال والجواب، وذلك بحسب الأشخاص، فمنهم مَنْ يُسأل عن بعض اعتقاداته، ومِنهم مَنْ يُسأَلُ عَنْ كُلُّها اها) . واختُلِفَ في اختصاصه بهذه الأُمّة ) ، ولا يُسألُ الأنبياء ولا الملائكة ولا الصدّيقون والمرابطونَ والشُّهَداءُ ومُلازِمُ قراءة «تباركَ كُلَّ لَيلةٍ، ومنْ قرأَ فِي مَرَضِ مَوتِه الإخلاص ثلاثا، والمبطونُ ومَنْ ماتَ في أيام الطاعون (٣) - ولو لم يُطْعَنْ - والمجنون والأبله.
وجزَمَ الجلال السيوطي بعدَم سؤالِ الأطفال، ويسألانِ الحِنَّ لتكليفهم وعُموم أدِلّةِ السؤال. وهذا السؤال هو فِتنةُ القبر.
And they ask everyone in his own tongue, according to the correct view, even if his limbs are torn apart, or beasts devoured him, or he was burned, crushed, and scattered in the air, for it is not improbable that Allah Most High creates life in him. And the states of the questioned are different: some are asked by both angels, some by one of them. Al-Qurtubi said: 'The reports differ concerning the manner of questioning and answering, according to the persons. Some are asked about some of their beliefs, and some are asked about all of them.' And there is disagreement about its being specific to this Ummah. And prophets are not asked, nor angels, nor the siddiqun, nor those stationed on the frontier (murabitun), nor martyrs, nor those who regularly recite 'Tabarak' every night, nor those who recited al-Ikhlas three times in their deathbed, nor the one who dies of a stomach disease, nor the one who dies during plague days even if not actually plague-stricken, nor the insane, nor the mentally deficient. And Jalal al-Suyuti affirmed decisively that children are not questioned. And the two angels question the jinn because they are obligated and due to the generality of the evidences of the questioning. And this questioning is the trial of the grave (fitnat al-qabr).
Source pages p. 161

Commentary
This passage covers several general rules. First, the questioning is in the person's own language, and it applies even if the body is completely destroyed, as God can recreate life. Second, the manner of questioning varies; some are asked by both angels, some by one, and questions may cover only part or all of one's beliefs. Third, there is a view that this questioning is specific to the Muslim Ummah, but this is disputed. Fourth, many categories are exempt from the questioning: prophets, angels, the truthful (siddiqun), frontier guards (murabitun), martyrs, those who regularly recite Surah Tabarak, those who recite al-Ikhlas on their deathbed, those who die of stomach disease, those who die during a plague, the insane, and the mentally deficient. Children are not questioned according to al-Suyuti. However, jinn are questioned because they are morally accountable. This questioning is called the 'trial of the grave' (fitnat al-qabr).

الأنبياء

الحن

Correction: The questioning is universal for all accountable beings, though many are exempted by divine mercy. The passage also mentions disagreement about specificity to this Ummah.

?

The Questioning in the Grave and Those Exempted
Imam al-Dardir describes the diversity of grave questioning and enumerates those exempted.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the questioning in the grave varies in manner and scope, and that several categories of people are exempted from it, including prophets, angels, and others.

Core Idea
Not everyone is questioned in the grave; many are exempted by Allah's mercy.

Imam al-Dardir now turns to a topic from the sam'iyyat: the questioning in the grave. He explains that this event is not uniform—it differs based on the person. He also lists those who are not questioned at all, and concludes by identifying this event as the fitnah of the grave. This passage highlights both the mercy of Allah and the variety of human conditions in the afterlife.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the grave questioning
Read the Arabic and translation carefully to understand the overall structure.
2
Identify the three main parts
Notice the passage begins with the differing conditions, then lists exceptions, and ends with a conclusion.
3
Examine the list of exempted groups
Count the categories and reflect on why each might be exempted.
4
Consider the fitnah of the grave
Understand that the questioning is a trial, but not a harmful one for the righteous.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأحوال المسئولين مختلفة: فمنهم من يسأله الملكان، ومنهم من يسأله أحدهما. قال القرطبي: اختلفت الأحاديث في كيفية السؤال والجواب، وذلك بحسب الأشخاص، فمنهم من يسأل عن بعض اعتقاداته، ومنهم من يسأل عن كلها. واختلف في اختصاصه بهذه الأمة، ولا يسأل الأنبياء ولا الملائكة ولا الصديقون والمرابطون والشهداء وملازم قراءة تبارك كل ليلة، ومن قرأ في مرض موته الإخلاص ثلاثا، والمبطون ومن مات في أيام الطاعون ولو لم يطعن، والمجنون والأبله. وجزم الجلال السيوطي بعدم سؤال الأطفال، ويسألان الجن لتكليفهم وعموم أدلة السؤال. وهذا السؤال هو فتنة القبر.
The conditions of those who are questioned are different: among them is one whom the two angels question, and among them is one whom only one of them questions. Al-Qurtubi said: 'The hadiths differ regarding the manner of the questioning and the answer, and that is according to the persons, for among them is one who is questioned about some of his beliefs, and among them is one who is questioned about all of them.' And there is disagreement concerning its being specific to this Ummah. And the prophets are not questioned, nor the angels, nor the siddiqun, nor the murabitun, nor the martyrs, nor the one who regularly recites Tabarak every night, nor the one who recites al-Ikhlas three times during his terminal illness, nor the one with dropsy, nor the one who dies during the days of plague even if he was not struck, nor the insane, nor the mentally deficient. And al-Jalal al-Suyuti decisively held that children are not questioned. And they [the angels] question the jinn because they are obligated and due to the generality of the proofs of questioning. And this questioning is the fitnah of the grave.
Source pages p. 161

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of the various states of those who are questioned by the angels in the grave. It begins by stating that there is diversity: some are questioned by both angels, some by only one. Imam al-Qurtubi is cited to show that hadiths vary on the specifics of the questioning depending on the individual; some are asked about a portion of their beliefs, others about all. The passage then notes a scholarly disagreement on whether the questioning is exclusive to this Ummah or applies to all nations. Next, a list of categories exempted from the questioning is given: prophets, angels, the siddiqun (truthful ones), the murabitun (those guarding frontiers), martyrs, those who habitually recite Surah Tabarak (al-Mulk) every night, those who recite Surah al-Ikhlas thrice in their final illness, those suffering from dropsy (al-mabtun), those who die during plague days even if not directly afflicted, the insane, and the mentally deficient (al-ablah). The passage then records that al-Suyuti ruled definitively that children are not questioned. However, the jinn are questioned because they are obligated beings (mukallafun) and the general proofs about the questioning apply to them. The passage concludes by identifying this questioning as the 'fitnah of the grave' – a test and trial, not necessarily harm for all.

فتنة القبر
الملكان
الصديقون
المرابطون
الشهداء
المبطون
المجنون
الأبله
الجن
الأطفال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Everyone who dies is subjected to a grueling interrogation in the grave.
Correction: The passage clarifies that prophets, angels, and many righteous individuals are exempted from the questioning altogether, and even for others, the questioning varies.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, who is exempted from the questioning in the grave?
A) All believers
B) Prophets, angels, siddiqun, and several others
C) Only prophets and angels
D) Only martyrs and prophets

Key Takeaway
The questioning in the grave is a varied trial, and many are exempted from it by Allah's mercy.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Imagine yourself at the moment of death, knowing the angels will soon arrive. Which exempted category do you hope to be in? What are you actively doing now to reach that rank?
?
The passage says that reciting Surah al-Mulk every night exempts one from grave questioning. Do you recite it nightly? If not, what is stopping you from securing this mercy for yourself?
?
Allah exempts the insane and mentally deficient from questioning. This shows His perfect justice and mercy. How does this awareness affect your gratitude for your own intellect, and how are you using it to prepare for your grave?

The Reality of Barzakh Punishment and Bliss
Definition of barzakh punishment/bliss and its locus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand what the punishment and bliss of the barzakh are, why they are referred to as 'grave', and that their locus is the soul and body together.

Core Idea
The barzakh's reward and punishment involve both soul and body, even without a physical grave.

Imam al-Dardir begins the section on Sam'iyyat by clarifying a central doctrine: the punishment and bliss of the intermediate state (barzakh) are real and experienced by both soul and body. Although commonly called 'grave punishment', this applies even if one is not buried. This lesson establishes the fundamental reality and its locus.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage defining barzakh punishment
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how the author clarifies that the term 'grave' is conventional.
The passage opens the third section on Sam'iyyat.
2
Understand the locus: soul and body
The passage states that the locus (mahall) of punishment and bliss is both soul and body together. It provides a reason: Allah can create a special life in body parts to perceive pain or pleasure.
This counters the idea that only the soul experiences it.
3
Reflect on the refutation of visible signs
The author emphasizes that this does not require visible movement or agitation, giving examples of those devoured by beasts or crucified. This shows the unseen nature of barzakh punishment.
Some might mistakenly expect a physical reaction.
4
Note the minority view
The passage mentions an alternative opinion: punishment is specific to the soul. Recognize that the author presents it as a lesser view.
The dominant view is soul and body together.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القسم الثالث: السمعيات. وكنعيم القبر وعذابه والمراد عذاب البرزخ ونعيمه، ولو لم يقبر، والتعبير بالقبر جري على الغالب، ومحله الروح والجسد جميعا، إذ لا مانع أن يخلق الله تعالى في جميع الأجزاء أو بعضها نوعا من الحياة قدر ما يدرك ألم العذاب أو لذة النعيم، وهذا لا يستلزم أن يتحرك أو يضطرب أو يرى أثر العذاب عليه، حتى إن من أكلته السباع أو صلب في الهواء يعذب وإن لم نطلع على ذلك، وقيل: مختص بالروح. والنعيم يكون للمؤمنين، والعذاب للكافرين ولعصاة المؤمنين من هذه الأمة وغيرها، وهو قسمان: دائم، وهو للكفار وبعض العصاة، ومنقطع وهو لبعض العصاة ممن خفت جرائمهم، وانقطاعه إما بسبب كصدقة أو دعاء، أو بلا سبب بل بمجرد العفو. ومن عذاب القبر ضغطته: وهي التقاء حافتيه حتى تختلف أضلاع الميت، ويختلف باختلاف العمل، حتى إن الصالح يضمه ضمة الأم الشفوقة على ولدها.
The third section: The Sam'iyyat. And the bliss and punishment of the grave: what is meant is the punishment and bliss of the barzakh, even if [the deceased] is not buried, and the expression 'grave' follows the customary. Its locus is the soul and the body together, as there is no impediment to Allah creating in all the parts or some of them a kind of life to the extent that it perceives the pain of punishment or the pleasure of bliss. And this does not necessitate that [the body] moves or is agitated or that any trace of punishment is seen upon it, so much so that one whom wild beasts have devoured or who was crucified in the air is punished even if we do not become aware of that. And it is said: it is specific to the soul. And bliss is for the believers, and punishment is for the disbelievers and for the disobedient believers from this Ummah and others. And it is of two kinds: eternal, and it is for the disbelievers and some of the disobedient; and temporary, and it is for some of the disobedient whose sins are light. And its cessation is either due to something like charity or supplication, or without any cause but by mere pardon. And from the punishment of the grave is its pressure: it is the meeting of its two sides until the ribs of the deceased become interlaced, and it varies according to deeds, so much so that the righteous [the pressure] embraces him like the embrace of a compassionate mother on her child.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage is a definition and classification of the punishment and bliss of the barzakh (intermediate state). It begins by clarifying that the term 'grave' is used conventionally; the reality is punishment and bliss in the barzakh even if one is not buried. The locus (mahall) is both the soul and the body together, because Allah can create a special type of life in some or all body parts sufficient to perceive pain or pleasure. This does not entail visible agitation—e.g., one eaten by beasts or crucified is still punished even if no physical movement is seen. An alternative view holds it is specific to the soul. Next, the passage states that bliss is for believers, punishment for disbelievers and sinful believers of this and other communities. Punishment is divided into: 1) eternal, for disbelievers and some sinful believers, and 2) temporary, for sinful believers with minor sins. The cessation of temporary punishment may occur due to intercession (charity, supplication) or purely through divine pardon. Finally, the passage describes 'pressure of the grave' (dagt al-qabr): the sides of the grave press until ribs interlace, and its intensity varies with deeds; for the righteous, it is like a mother's gentle embrace.

Key Terms
عذاب القبر
نعيم القبر
البرزخ
محل العذاب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The punishment of the grave happens only to the body in a physical grave.
Correction: The punishment and bliss occur in the barzakh for both soul and body, even if the body is not buried, and no visible signs are necessary.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the locus of punishment and bliss in the barzakh?
A) Only the soul
B) Only the body
C) Both soul and body together
D) Neither, as it is purely spiritual

Key Takeaway
The punishment and bliss of the barzakh involve both soul and body, and occur even without a grave, with no need for visible signs.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were to die tonight and enter the barzakh, what would you expect to experience? How does knowing that your body will also feel punishment or bliss change your view of your actions today?
?
This lesson teaches that even if your body is destroyed or lost, Allah can still make it feel. How should this affect your fear of punishment and hope for reward? Are you living as if the barzakh is real and imminent?
?
Do you truly believe that every deed—seen or unseen—will be accounted for in the barzakh? What will you do differently starting today to prepare for that reality?

Eternal and Temporary Punishment in the Barzakh
Classification of punishment into eternal/temporary and description of grave pressure.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will distinguish between eternal and temporary punishment in the barzakh, understand how temporary punishment ends, and learn about the pressure of the grave.

Core Idea
Punishment in the grave is either eternal for disbelievers or temporary for sinful believers, ending by mercy or intercession.

Having established the reality of barzakh punishment, Imam al-Dardir now explains its two divisions: eternal and temporary. He also describes the 'pressure of the grave' and how its intensity varies with deeds. This lesson clarifies the scope of divine justice and mercy in the intermediate state.

Guided Path
1
Read the classification of punishment
Read the Arabic passage and translation focusing on the two divisions of punishment: eternal and temporary.
The passage begins with bliss for believers and punishment for disbelievers and sinners.
2
Identify who receives eternal punishment
Eternal punishment is for disbelievers and some sinful believers. Understand that this is a permanent state in the barzakh.
This does not contradict eventual punishment in Hell.
3
Identify who receives temporary punishment
Temporary punishment is for sinful believers with light sins. It ends either through means (charity, supplication) or by pure pardon.
Note that cessation can be without cause.
4
Study the pressure of the grave
The passage describes a specific punishment: the grave presses its sides until ribs interlace. This pressure varies with deeds, with the righteous experiencing a gentle embrace.
This shows punishment is not uniform.

The Life of Martyrs in the Grave
Imam al-Dardir asserts the real life of martyrs, citing Quran and noting modality unknown.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that martyrs are truly alive in the barzakh, enjoying Paradise, based on the Quran, while accepting that the modality of this life is unknown.

Core Idea
Martyrs are truly alive in the grave, though how remains a mystery.

In this lesson, Imam al-Dardir discusses the life of martyrs after death. He affirms that they are not merely spiritually alive but experience real pleasures in Paradise, citing the Quran. However, he cautions that the exact nature of this life is beyond human comprehension. We will explore the evidence and the key points of this belief.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the passage is concise but packed with theological claims.
2
Identify the definition and proof
Find how Imam al-Dardir defines martyrs and what Quranic verse he uses as evidence. Note the specific actions attributed to them (eating, drinking, enjoying).
The definition is specific: those killed in jihad for Allah's word.
3
Understand the qualification
The passage ends with a crucial point: the kayfiyya (modality) of this life is unknown. Ask yourself why this qualification is necessary for correct belief.
This prevents trying to conceptualise what we cannot grasp.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكحياة الشهداء، وهم من قتلوا في جهاد الكفار لإعلاء كلمة الله تعالى، حتى إنهم يأكلون ويشربون ويتنعمون في الجنة. قال تعالى: {ولا تحسبن الذين قتلوا في سبيل الله أمواتا بل أحياء عند ربهم يرزقون}. وإن لم تعلم كيفية هذه الحياة، إذ هي غير معقولة لأكثر البشر.
And the life of the martyrs: they are those who are killed in jihad against the disbelievers to elevate the word of Allah, so much so that they eat, drink, and enjoy themselves in Paradise. Allah said: {And do not think that those who are killed in the way of Allah are dead; rather, they are alive with their Lord, provided for.} Even if the modality of this life is not known, as it is incomprehensible to most humans.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal statement on the life of martyrs in the barzakh. It defines martyrs as those killed specifically in jihad against disbelievers for the sake of Allah's word. It affirms that they are alive in a real sense: they eat, drink, and enjoy Paradise. The Quranic verse (Al 'Imran 3:169) is cited as evidence: they are not dead but alive and provided for by their Lord. The passage then adds a crucial qualification: the modality (kayfiyya) of this life is unknown and beyond the comprehension of most humans. Thus, one must affirm the reality without attempting to conceptualize its nature. This balances literal acceptance with recognition of divine mystery.

Key Terms
حياة الشهداء
الشهداء
الجهاد
الكيفية
غير معقولة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Martyrs are dead like ordinary people; their life is only symbolic or spiritual.
Correction: The Quran explicitly says they are alive and provided for, and Imam al-Dardir affirms they eat, drink, and enjoy Paradise in a real sense.

Checkpoint

A) It is only metaphorical
B) Its modality is not known and is beyond most humans
C) They are actually dead and only their souls live
D) Only prophets can understand it

Key Takeaway
Martyrs are truly alive in the barzakh, enjoying Paradise, though the modality remains unknown.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

Introduction to Grave Punishment and Bliss
Dardeer introduces the Samiyyat and defines grave punishment as barzakh punishment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meaning of the 'samiyyat' and that the punishment and bliss of the grave refer to the barzakh, with the term 'grave' being the common expression.

Core Idea
Grave punishment is really barzakh punishment, whether buried or not.

Dardeer begins the section on Samiyyat by clarifying the subject: the punishment and bliss of the grave. He immediately corrects a potential misunderstanding by explaining that the intended meaning is the punishment of the barzakh (the intermediate state), even if a person is not buried. The term 'grave' is used as it is the most common scenario.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice how the author defines the topic.
2
Identify the scope
Identify that the passage is introducing the third section (Samiyyat) and specifying the topic: punishment and bliss of the grave, which is actually the barzakh.
3
Reflect on the term 'grave'
Consider why the author uses 'grave' despite the reality extending to all deceased. This will help you understand the importance of the barzakh concept.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القسم الثالث: السمعيات. وكنعيم القبر وعذابه والمراد عذابُ البرزخ ونعيمه، ولو لم يُقبرُ، والتعبير بالقبر جري على الغالب، ومحلهُ الرُّوحُ والجسَدُ جميعًا، إذ لا مانع أنْ يخلق الله تعالى في جميع الأجزاء أو بعضها نَوعًا مِنَ الحياةِ قدْرَ ما يُدرك ألم العذاب أو لذة النعيم، وهذا لا يستلزم أن يتحرَّك أو يضطرب أو يُرى أثَرُ العذاب عليه، حتى إِنَّ مَنْ أَكَلتُه السِّباعُ أو صلب في الهواءِ يُعذِّبُ وإِن لم نطلع على ذلك، وقيل: مختص بالروح. والنعيم يكون للمؤمنين، والعذاب للكافرين ولِعُصاةِ المؤمنين مِنْ هذه الأمة وغيرها، وهو قِسمان: دائم، وهو للكُفَّارِ وبعض العُصاةِ، ومُنقطع وهو لبعض العُصاةِ مِمَّنْ خَفَّتْ جرائمهم، وانقطاعه: إما جرائمهم، وانقطاعه إما بسبب كصدقة أو دعاء، أو بلا سبب بل بمُجرَّدِ العفو. ومِنْ عذابِ القبرِ ضغطتُه: وهي التقاء حافتيه حتى تختلفَ أضلاعُ الميت، ويختلف باختلافِ العمل، حتى إنّ الصالحَ يَضُمُّه ضمّةَ الأم الشفوقة على ولدها.
The third section: The Samiyyat. And like the bliss of the grave and its punishment, and the intended is the punishment of the Barzakh and its bliss, even if he was not buried, and the expression 'grave' is used as the common case. Its place is the soul and the body together, because there is nothing preventing Allah from creating in all the parts or some of them a type of life enough to perceive the pain of punishment or the pleasure of bliss. This does not necessitate that he move or be agitated or that the effect of punishment be seen upon him, so much so that indeed one whom beasts have eaten or who was crucified in the air is punished even if we do not witness that. And it was said: specific to the soul. Bliss is for the believers, and punishment is for the disbelievers and for sinful believers from this nation and others. It is of two kinds: permanent, which is for the disbelievers and some sinners, and temporary, which is for some sinners whose crimes are light. Its cessation is either due to charity or supplication, or without cause but merely by pardon. And from the punishment of the grave is its squeeze: which is the meeting of its two sides until the ribs of the dead become interlaced, and it varies according to the deed, so much so that indeed the righteous person it embraces like the embrace of a compassionate mother over her child.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage is a definition and explanation of the punishment and bliss of the grave. It begins by stating that the intended meaning is the punishment of the barzakh (intermediate state) and its bliss, even if the person is not buried; the term 'grave' is used because it is the common case. Then it explains that its location is both the soul and the body together, because nothing prevents Allah from creating in some or all of the body parts a type of life sufficient to perceive the pain or pleasure. This does not imply movement or visible effects, so even those eaten by beasts or crucified are punished. Some say it is specific to the soul. Then it states that bliss is for the believers, punishment for disbelievers and sinful believers, and it is of two types: permanent (for disbelievers) and temporary (for some sinners with light sins), and its cessation may be due to charity, supplication, or mere pardon. Finally, it mentions the 'squeeze of the grave' where the two sides meet until the ribs interlock, varying according to one's deeds.

Key Terms
السَّمْعِيَّات
عَذَابُ الْقَبْرِ
نَعِيمُ الْقَبْرِ
الْبَرْزَخُ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that only those buried in graves experience punishment or bliss.
Correction: The punishment and bliss are of the barzakh, experienced by all deceased, regardless of burial.

Checkpoint
According to Dardeer, what is the intended meaning of 'punishment of the grave'?
A) Punishment that occurs only in the grave itself
B) The punishment of the barzakh
C) Punishment only for the soul
D) Punishment only for the body

Key Takeaway
The punishment and bliss of the grave refer to the barzakh, experienced by all deceased, and the term 'grave' is a common expression.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?

The Location of Punishment and Bliss
Dardeer explains the location of punishment as both soul and body together.

Core Idea
Both soul and body share the experience, with Allah creating life enough for perception.

After defining the scope, Dardeer addresses a key question: where does the punishment or bliss occur? He asserts that it involves both soul and body together, explaining how Allah can create a type of life in the body parts sufficient to perceive pain or pleasure without requiring movement or visible signs.

Guided Path

4

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القسم الثالث: السمعيات. وكنعيم القبر وعذابه والمراد عذابُ البرزخ ونعيمه، ولو لم يُقبرُ، والتعبير بالقبر جري على الغالب، ومحلهُ الرُّوحُ والجسَدُ جميعًا، إذ لا مانع أنْ يخلق الله تعالى في جميع الأجزاء أو بعضها نَوعًا مِنَ الحياةِ قدْرَ ما يُدرك ألم العذاب أو لذة النعيم، وهذا لا يستلزم أن يتحرَّك أو يضطرب أو يُرى أثَرُ العذاب عليه، حتى إِنَّ مَنْ أَكَلتُه السِّباعُ أو صلب في الهواءِ يُعذِّبُ وإِن لم نطلع على ذلك، وقيل: مختص بالروح. والنعيم يكون للمؤمنين، والعذاب للكافرين ولِعُصاةِ المؤمنين مِنْ هذه الأمة وغيرها، وهو قِسمان: دائم، وهو للكُفَّارِ وبعض العُصاةِ، ومُنقطع وهو لبعض العُصاةِ مِمَّنْ خَفَّتْ جرائمهم، وانقطاعه: إما جرائمهم، وانقطاعه إما بسبب كصدقة أو دعاء، أو بلا سبب بل بمُجرَّدِ العفو. ومِنْ عذابِ القبرِ ضغطتُه: وهي التقاء حافتيه حتى تختلفَ أضلاعُ الميت، ويختلف باختلافِ العمل، حتى إنّ الصالحَ يَضُمُّه ضمّةَ الأم الشفوقة على ولدها.
The third section: The Samiyyat. And like the bliss of the grave and its punishment, and the intended is the punishment of the Barzakh and its bliss, even if he was not buried, and the expression 'grave' is used as the common case. Its place is the soul and the body together, because there is nothing preventing Allah from creating in all the parts or some of them a type of life enough to perceive the pain of punishment or the pleasure of bliss. This does not necessitate that he move or be agitated or that the effect of punishment be seen upon him, so much so that indeed one whom beasts have eaten or who was crucified in the air is punished even if we do not witness that. And it was said: specific to the soul. Bliss is for the believers, and punishment is for the disbelievers and for sinful believers from this nation and others. It is of two kinds: permanent, which is for the disbelievers and some sinners, and temporary, which is for some sinners whose crimes are light. Its cessation is either due to charity or supplication, or without cause but merely by pardon. And from the punishment of the grave is its squeeze: which is the meeting of its two sides until the ribs of the dead become interlaced, and it varies according to the deed, so much so that indeed the righteous person it embraces like the embrace of a compassionate mother over her child.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage is a definition and explanation of the punishment and bliss of the grave. It begins by stating that the intended meaning is the punishment of the barzakh (intermediate state) and its bliss, even if the person is not buried; the term 'grave' is used because it is the common case. Then it explains that its location is both the soul and the body together, because nothing prevents Allah from creating in some or all of the body parts a type of life sufficient to perceive the pain or pleasure. This does not imply movement or visible effects, so even those eaten by beasts or crucified are punished. Some say it is specific to the soul. Then it states that bliss is for the believers, punishment for disbelievers and sinful believers, and it is of two types: permanent (for disbelievers) and temporary (for some sinners with light sins), and its cessation may be due to charity, supplication, or mere pardon. Finally, it mentions the 'squeeze of the grave' where the two sides meet until the ribs interlock, varying according to one's deeds.

Key Terms
مَحَلُّ الْعَذَابِ
الرُّوحُ
الْجَسَدُ
نَوْعٌ مِنَ الْحَيَاةِ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that only the soul experiences the punishment, or only the body.
Correction: Dardeer affirms it is both soul and body together, with Allah creating a special life for perception.

Checkpoint
According to Dardeer, what is the location of the punishment of the grave?
A) Only the soul
B) Only the body
C) Both the soul and the body
D) Neither, it is purely spiritual

Key Takeaway
The punishment and bliss of the grave affect both soul and body, without requiring visible physical signs.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you reflect on the fact that the punishment of the grave affects both soul and body without visible signs, does it make you think differently about the hidden sins you commit? What one hidden sin will you repent from tonight, specifically asking Allah to protect you from its consequences in the grave?
?
If Allah can create life in a decaying body to feel pain, are you living as if every action—even those unseen—has real, tangible consequences? What is one habit you will change today because you now know that the grave sees what the world does not?
?
The passage mentions that even those eaten by beasts are punished. Does this give you awe of Allah's power or fear for your own state? How will you use that feeling to change your salah tonight, making it a true plea for mercy in the grave?

Types of Punishment and Bliss: Permanent and Temporary
Dardeer classifies the recipients and types of punishment/bliss.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that bliss is for believers, punishment for disbelievers and sinful believers, and that punishment is of two types: permanent and temporary, with cessation possible through charity, supplication, or pardon.

Core Idea
Punishment varies: permanent for disbelievers, temporary for some sinful believers, and can end through intercession.

Dardeer now categorizes the recipients of bliss and punishment. He specifies that bliss is exclusively for believers, while punishment applies to disbelievers and sinful believers. He then divides punishment into two kinds: permanent (for disbelievers and some sinners) and temporary (for those with light sins), explaining how temporary punishment can cease.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the categories: bliss for believers, punishment for disbelievers and sinful believers.
2
Identify the two kinds of punishment
Find where Dardeer says punishment is divided into permanent and temporary. Understand who each applies to.
3
Learn about cessation of punishment
Note the three ways temporary punishment ends: due to charity or supplication, or through mere pardon.
4
Reflect on the scope
Understand that sinful believers from this Ummah and others may experience temporary punishment.

The Squeeze of the Grave
Dardeer defines the squeeze of the grave and its variation based on deeds.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the reality of the squeeze of the grave (ضغطة القبر), its description, and how it varies according to one's deeds.

Core Idea
The grave squeeze varies; for the righteous it is a loving embrace.

Dardeer concludes this section by describing a specific aspect of grave punishment: the squeeze. He defines it as the meeting of the two sides of the grave until the ribs interlace, and emphasizes that it differs based on one's actions—for the righteous, it is like the embrace of a compassionate mother.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Focus on the definition of the squeeze.
2
Understand the variation
Note that the squeeze is not uniform; it changes according to the person's deeds.
3
Reflect on the example
Consider the beautiful analogy: for the righteous, it feels like a mother's embrace. This shows that even the squeeze can be a form of mercy.

The Life of Martyrs: Real but Mysterious
Dardeer defines martyrs and describes their life with Quranic proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that martyrs enjoy a real, physical life in paradise after death, though its precise nature is beyond human comprehension.

Core Idea
Martyrs are alive with Allah, enjoying paradise, but the how remains unknown.

Dardeer now discusses the life of martyrs, a topic that raises questions about the nature of life after death. He defines who qualifies as a martyr, cites the Quranic proof, and emphasizes that their life is real yet incomprehensible. Let's explore his teaching.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the translation. Notice how Dardeer starts with definition and immediately gives the Quranic verse.
2
Identify the definition and its scope
Find the definition of martyr and note the scholarly differences on who qualifies. Note the inclusion of those killed for truth, not just battlefield.
Al-Qurtubi and al-Nawawi expand the definition.
3
Understand the nature of their life
Reflect on the statement that martyrs have a real life with eating and drinking, but its modality is unknown. This is a matter of faith.
Do not confuse this with mere spiritual life.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكحياةِ الشُّهَداءِ ، وهم مَنْ قُتِلوا في جهادِ الكفّار لإعلاء كلمة الله تعالى) ، حتى إنهم يأكلون ويشربون ويتنعمون في الجنّة. قال تعالى ﴿وَلاَ تَحْسَبَنَّ الَّذِينَ قُتِلُوا فِي سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ أَمْوَاتاً بَلْ أَحْيَاءٌ عِندَ رَبِّهِمْ يُرْزَقُونَ)). وإِنْ لَّمْ تُعلَمْ كيفيّةُ هذه الحياةِ، إِذْ هي غير معقولة لأكثر البشَرِ (۳). (1) ظاهر كلام العلماء في قصر تعريف الشهيد على من قتل في حرب الكفار، وهذا لكونه فيه أتم أو لكونه مقطوعا له بالشهادة في ذلك، ولكن صرح الإمام القرطبي بأن كل مقتول على الحق هذا سبيله. وقال النووي: وهذا الفضل وإن كان الظاهر أنه في قتال الكفار لكن يدخل فيه من جرح في سبيل الله في قتال البغاة وقطاع الطريق، وفي إقامة الأمر بالمعروف والنهي عن المنكر. (۲) سورة آل عمران: الآية ١٦٩ (۳) الظاهر اتصاف هيكل الشهداء بالحياة الحقيقية، وبه جزم بعض المحققين، كذلك الظاهر أنهم يرزقون كما يرزق الأحياء بالأكل والشرب واللباس وغيرها وهو أمر ممكن، ولكنه غير مكيف ولا معقول للبشر، فيجب الإيمان بحياة الشهداء على ما جاء به ظاهر الشرع، ولا ينبغي أن يقال عن حياة الشهداء إنها للروح، لأن هذه ثابتة لجميع الأموات بالاتفاق. وسُمّوا شُهَداءَ؛ لأنَّ أرواحهم شهدتْ دار السلام، أي: حضَرتها ودخلتها، بخلاف غيرهم، فإنّه لا يدخُلُها إلا يَومَ القيامة، أو لأنَّ الله وملائكته شهدا لهـ بالموافاة (١). (۱) وقال ابن الأنباري: لأن الله وملائكته يشهدون له بالجنة، فمعنى شهيد: مشهود له. وقيل: لأنه يشهد عند خروج روحه ما له من الثواب والكرامة، وقيل: لأن عليه شاهدا وهو دمه، فإنه يبعث وجرحه يثعب دما، وقيل: لسقوطه على الأرض والأرض شاهدة وشهيد على وزن فعيل بمعنى فاعل، أي شاهد لدار السلام، وقيل: بمعنى مفعول أي مشهود له.
And like the life of martyrs, and they are those who were killed in jihad against the disbelievers for the elevation of the word of Allah, so much so that they eat and drink and enjoy in paradise. Allah said: 'And do not think that those who were killed in the way of Allah are dead; rather they are alive with their Lord, receiving provision.' And if the modality of this life is not known, for it is inconceivable to most humans. (3) (1) The apparent words of the scholars restrict the definition of the martyr to one killed in war against disbelievers, and this because it is more complete or because martyrdom is certain in that case, but Imam al-Qurtubi stated that every one killed upon the truth is in this way. And al-Nawawi said: This virtue, even if apparent it is in fighting disbelievers, yet it includes one wounded in the way of Allah in fighting rebels and highway robbers, and in establishing enjoining good and forbidding evil. (2) Surah Al 'Imran: verse 169. (3) The apparent is that these martyrs are described with real life, and some investigators affirmed it, likewise the apparent is that they are provided as the living are provided with eating, drinking, clothing and other things, and it is possible, but it is unqualified and inconceivable to humans, so faith in the life of martyrs is obligatory according to what the apparent of the Shari'a has brought, and it should not be said about the life of martyrs that it is for the soul, because this is established for all the dead by consensus. And they were called martyrs because their souls witnessed (shahidat) the Abode of Peace, i.e. they attended it and entered it, unlike others, for he does not enter it except on the Day of Resurrection, or because Allah and His angels testified (shahida) for him with arrival (to paradise). (1) And Ibn al-Anbari said: Because Allah and His angels testify for him with paradise, so the meaning of 'shahid' is one for whom testimony is given. And it was said: Because he witnesses at the exit of his soul what he has of reward and honor. And it was said: Because upon him is a witness, which is his blood, for he is resurrected with his wound flowing blood. And it was said: Because of his falling to the ground, and the ground is a witness. And 'shahid' is on the pattern of fa'il in the sense of fa', i.e. a witness to the Abode of Peace, and it was said: in the sense of maf'ul, i.e. one for whom testimony is given.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage discusses the life of martyrs. It begins by defining martyrs as those killed in jihad against disbelievers for the elevation of Allah's word, and that they eat, drink, and enjoy in paradise, quoting verse 3:169. Their life is incomprehensible to most. Then it notes a definition issue: some scholars restrict martyrdom to battlefield, but al-Qurtubi includes all killed on truth. Then it affirms that martyrs have real life, not just spiritual, though its modality is unknown. Then it gives reasons for the name 'shahid' (martyr): their souls witness (shahadat) the Abode of Peace (paradise) and enter it before others, or that Allah and His angels testify for them. Additional opinions from Ibn al-Anbari etc. are cited.

Key Terms
شهيد
حياة الشهداء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the life of martyrs is purely spiritual, akin to the continued existence of the soul.
Correction: Dardeer explicitly states that the life is real with physical sustenance, and it should not be reduced to spiritual life, as that is common to all dead.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Martyrs are alive with Allah, enjoying physical pleasures in paradise, but the exact nature of that life is known only to Allah.

?
You read that martyrs are those killed for the elevation of Allah's word. What are you willing to sacrifice for that cause? Is your life aligned with that standard, or are you holding back? Commit to one concrete action this week that shows you value Allah's word above your comfort.

Why Martyrs Are Called Shuhada'
Dardeer enumerates reasons for naming martyrs as shuhada'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the various etymological reasons for why those killed in Allah's path are called 'shuhada'' (martyrs).

Core Idea
Martyrs are named for witnessing paradise or being testified for by Allah.

After discussing the life of martyrs, Dardeer now explains why they are called 'shuhada''. He gives multiple linguistic and theological reasons, all rooted in the root word 'shahada' (to witness). Let's explore these explanations.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and find the reasons
Read the Arabic and translation. List each reason given for the name 'shahid'.
There are at least four distinct opinions.
2
Analyze the root meaning
Notice how all reasons relate to the root 'shahada'. Identify which reason Dardeer mentions first, and which are from other scholars.
Dardeer gives his own preferred reason before quoting others.
3
Reflect on the depth
Consider how these reasons enrich our understanding of martyrdom. Why do you think there are multiple interpretations?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكحياةِ الشُّهَداءِ ، وهم مَنْ قُتِلوا في جهادِ الكفّار لإعلاء كلمة الله تعالى) ، حتى إنهم يأكلون ويشربون ويتنعمون في الجنّة. قال تعالى ﴿وَلاَ تَحْسَبَنَّ الَّذِينَ قُتِلُوا فِي سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ أَمْوَاتاً بَلْ أَحْيَاءٌ عِندَ رَبِّهِمْ يُرْزَقُونَ)). وإِنْ لَّمْ تُعلَمْ كيفيّةُ هذه الحياةِ، إِذْ هي غير معقولة لأكثر البشَرِ (۳). (1) ظاهر كلام العلماء في قصر تعريف الشهيد على من قتل في حرب الكفار، وهذا لكونه فيه أتم أو لكونه مقطوعا له بالشهادة في ذلك، ولكن صرح الإمام القرطبي بأن كل مقتول على الحق هذا سبيله. وقال النووي: وهذا الفضل وإن كان الظاهر أنه في قتال الكفار لكن يدخل فيه من جرح في سبيل الله في قتال البغاة وقطاع الطريق، وفي إقامة الأمر بالمعروف والنهي عن المنكر. (۲) سورة آل عمران: الآية ١٦٩ (۳) الظاهر اتصاف هيكل الشهداء بالحياة الحقيقية، وبه جزم بعض المحققين، كذلك الظاهر أنهم يرزقون كما يرزق الأحياء بالأكل والشرب واللباس وغيرها وهو أمر ممكن، ولكنه غير مكيف ولا معقول للبشر، فيجب الإيمان بحياة الشهداء على ما جاء به ظاهر الشرع، ولا ينبغي أن يقال عن حياة الشهداء إنها للروح، لأن هذه ثابتة لجميع الأموات بالاتفاق. وسُمّوا شُهَداءَ؛ لأنَّ أرواحهم شهدتْ دار السلام، أي: حضَرتها ودخلتها، بخلاف غيرهم، فإنّه لا يدخُلُها إلا يَومَ القيامة، أو لأنَّ الله وملائكته شهدا لهـ بالموافاة (١). (۱) وقال ابن الأنباري: لأن الله وملائكته يشهدون له بالجنة، فمعنى شهيد: مشهود له. وقيل: لأنه يشهد عند خروج روحه ما له من الثواب والكرامة، وقيل: لأن عليه شاهدا وهو دمه، فإنه يبعث وجرحه يثعب دما، وقيل: لسقوطه على الأرض والأرض شاهدة وشهيد على وزن فعيل بمعنى فاعل، أي شاهد لدار السلام، وقيل: بمعنى مفعول أي مشهود له.
And like the life of martyrs, and they are those who were killed in jihad against the disbelievers for the elevation of the word of Allah, so much so that they eat and drink and enjoy in paradise. Allah said: 'And do not think that those who were killed in the way of Allah are dead; rather they are alive with their Lord, receiving provision.' And if the modality of this life is not known, for it is inconceivable to most humans. (3) (1) The apparent words of the scholars restrict the definition of the martyr to one killed in war against disbelievers, and this because it is more complete or because martyrdom is certain in that case, but Imam al-Qurtubi stated that every one killed upon the truth is in this way. And al-Nawawi said: This virtue, even if apparent it is in fighting disbelievers, yet it includes one wounded in the way of Allah in fighting rebels and highway robbers, and in establishing enjoining good and forbidding evil. (2) Surah Al 'Imran: verse 169. (3) The apparent is that these martyrs are described with real life, and some investigators affirmed it, likewise the apparent is that they are provided as the living are provided with eating, drinking, clothing and other things, and it is possible, but it is unqualified and inconceivable to humans, so faith in the life of martyrs is obligatory according to what the apparent of the Shari'a has brought, and it should not be said about the life of martyrs that it is for the soul, because this is established for all the dead by consensus. And they were called martyrs because their souls witnessed (shahidat) the Abode of Peace, i.e. they attended it and entered it, unlike others, for he does not enter it except on the Day of Resurrection, or because Allah and His angels testified (shahida) for him with arrival (to paradise). (1) And Ibn al-Anbari said: Because Allah and His angels testify for him with paradise, so the meaning of 'shahid' is one for whom testimony is given. And it was said: Because he witnesses at the exit of his soul what he has of reward and honor. And it was said: Because upon him is a witness, which is his blood, for he is resurrected with his wound flowing blood. And it was said: Because of his falling to the ground, and the ground is a witness. And 'shahid' is on the pattern of fa'il in the sense of fa', i.e. a witness to the Abode of Peace, and it was said: in the sense of maf'ul, i.e. one for whom testimony is given.

Commentary
This passage discusses the life of martyrs. It begins by defining martyrs as those killed in jihad against disbelievers for the elevation of Allah's word, and that they eat, drink, and enjoy in paradise, quoting verse 3:169. Their life is incomprehensible to most. Then it notes a definition issue: some scholars restrict martyrdom to battlefield, but al-Qurtubi includes all killed on truth. Additional opinions from Ibn al-Anbari etc. are cited.

The Taking of the Books of Deeds on Judgment Day
Dardeer explains how the books of deeds are given to the righteous and the wicked.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the books of deeds are given to the righteous and the wicked on Judgment Day, including the specific process involving the treasury under the Throne and the wind.

Core Idea
The books of deeds are physically given to each person, believers with the right hand and disbelievers from behind.

Imam Dardeer describes the dramatic event on Judgment Day when every accountable person receives their record of deeds. This passage quotes the Quran and explains the mechanism by which the scrolls are delivered to each individual. The description emphasizes the physical reality of this event, countering any notion of mere symbolism.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then the translation. Notice the Quranic quotes and the process described.
Focus on the distinction between the exceptions and the general rule.
2
Identify the exceptions
Note that prophets and the seventy thousand who enter paradise without account do not receive books in this manner.
Why are these groups exempt? Ponder this question.
3
Understand the storage and delivery process
Scrolls are joined into one, stored under the Throne, then a wind brings them to each person's neck on Judgment Day.
This underscores the meticulous divine arrangement.
4
Contrast the believer and disbeliever
Believers receive their book in the right hand; disbelievers take it from behind after their chest is pierced.
This physical detail highlights the honor or humiliation.
5
Reflect on the special mention of Umar and Abu Bakr
Umar is the first to receive his book with the right hand; Abu Bakr leads the seventy thousand without account.
Their high status is affirmed in this context.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكأخذ العباد المكلفين منَ الثَّقَلَين في المحْشَر - ما عدا الأنبياء والسَّبعين ألفا الذين يدخلون الجنة بغير حساب- كُتبهم التي كَتَبَتْ فيها الملائكةُ الحفَظَةُ أعمالهم التي صدرت عنهم في الدُّنيا، بالأيمان والشمائل ﴿فَأَمَّا مَنْ أُوتِ كتبهُ بيمينه يُحَاسَبُ حِسَاباً يَسِيراً * وَيَنقَلِبُ إِلَى أَهْلِهِ مَسْرُوراً * وَأَمَّا مَنْ أُوتِيَ كِتُبُهُ وَرَاءَ ظَهْرهِ : فَسَوْفَ يَدْعُوا تُبُوراً * وَيَصْلَى سَعِيراً ) (۲). فَسَوْفَ وحاصل ما قيل في ذلك: أنَّ صحائف الأيام والليالي توصل حتى تكون صحيفةً واحدةً، وقيل: يُنسَخُ ما في جميعها في صحيفة واحدة، فإذا ماتَ العَبدُ جُعِلتْ في خزانة تحت العرش، حتى إذا كان يَومُ القيامةِ والناسُ في الموقفِ بَعَثَ الله تعالى ريحا فتطيرها من تلك الخزانة، فلا تخطى صحيفةٌ عُنق صاحبها، ثُمَّ تَأخُذُها الملائكةُ مِنَ الأعناق فيعطونها لهم في أيديهم على حسب حالِهِم مِنْ إيمان أو كُفْرِ، فالمؤمنُ يعطى كتابه بيمينه، والكافرُ بشماله، ويثقَبُ  َصدرُه فيُدخِلُ يَدَه اليُسْرى فيه ويأخُذُ كِتابَه مِنْ وراءِ ظَهرِه. وأولُ مَنْ يَأخُذُ كِتابه بيمينه على الإطلاقِ عُمَرُ بنُ الخَطَّابِ رَضِي الله عنه وله شعاعٌ عَنْهُ كالشمس، وأما أبو بكر فهو رئيس السبعين ألفا الذين يدخلون الجنّةَ بغَيرِ حِساب. (۲) سورة الانشقاق: الآيات ۷-۱۲
And like the taking of the accountable servants from the two heavy ones (jinn and humans) in the gathering place – except the prophets and the seventy thousand who enter paradise without account – their books which the guardian angels wrote in them, their deeds that issued from them in this world, with the right hands and the left hands: 'Then as for he who is given his book in his right hand, he will be judged with an easy account and return to his family delighted. But as for he who is given his book behind his back, he will call for destruction and enter a blazing fire.' (2) 'So he will call' – and the summary of what was said about that: that the scrolls of days and nights are joined so that they become one scroll, and it was said: what is in all of them is copied into one scroll. So when the servant dies, it is placed in a treasury under the Throne. Until when it is the Day of Resurrection and the people are in the gathering place, Allah sends a wind that flies them from that treasury, and no scroll misses the neck of its owner. Then the angels take them from the necks and give them to them in their hands according to their state of faith or disbelief. So the believer is given his book in his right hand, and the disbeliever in his left hand, and his chest is pierced, and he inserts his left hand into it and takes his book from behind his back. And the first person to take his book with his right hand absolutely is 'Umar ibn al-Khattab, may Allah be pleased with him, and there radiates from him a light like the sun. As for Abu Bakr, he is the leader of the seventy thousand who enter paradise without account. (2) Surah al-Inshiqaq: verses 7-12.
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage describes the event of the taking of the books of deeds. It states that all accountable beings from humans and jinn (except prophets and the seventy thousand who enter paradise without account) will receive their books. The books contain their deeds recorded by the guardian angels. It quotes Surah al-Inshiqaq about those who receive with right hand and those given behind the back. Then it explains that the scrolls of days and nights are joined into one, or combined into one scroll. After death, the scroll is placed in a treasury under the Throne. On Judgment Day, Allah sends a wind that brings each scroll to its owner's neck, then angels take them and give them according to faith: the believer with his right hand, the disbeliever with his left hand, and the disbeliever's chest is pierced so he takes it from behind. The first to take his book with his right hand is Umar ibn al-Khattab, while Abu Bakr is the leader of the seventy thousand who enter paradise without account.

Why Martyrs Are Called Shuhada'
Explains multiple interpretations for why martyrs are called shuhada'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the multiple interpretations for why martyrs are called shuhada' and how the term is rooted in the concept of 'witnessing'.

Core Idea
Martyrs are called shuhada' because they witness Paradise or are witnessed for by Allah.

Have you ever wondered why those who die in Allah's path are called 'shuhada' (martyrs)? The term is rich in meaning, deriving from the root 'shahida' (to witness). In this passage, Imam Dardir presents several explanations that reveal both the spiritual privilege of martyrs and the beauty of the Arabic language. Let's explore these interpretations together.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage slowly, then the English translation. Notice the multiple explanations introduced by 'because' or 'and it is said'.
There is a footnote (1) at the end of the first sentence that refers to further explanations by Ibn al-Anbari.
2
Identify the first two main explanations
The passage begins with two main reasons: 1) martyrs' souls immediately enter Dar al-Salam, and 2) Allah and His angels testify for them. Understand the distinction: the first focuses on the martyr's own witnessing, the second on being the object of testimony.
3
Study Ibn al-Anbari's linguistic points
Ibn al-Anbari adds that the word 'shahid' can mean 'one for whom testimony is given' (passive sense). Also note the morphological explanation that 'shahid' can be active (witness) or passive (witnessed for).
4
Review the remaining explanations
The passage lists additional reasons: the martyr witnesses his own reward, his blood testifies against him, and the earth testifies as he falls. Think about how each reason connects to the concept of witnessing.
Some explanations emphasize the martyr as a witness, others as one witnessed.
5
Answer the checkpoint question
Test your understanding by answering the multiple-choice question based solely on this passage.
This will help you remember the first explanation given.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وسُمّوا شُهَداءَ؛ لأنَّ أرواحهم شهدتْ دار السلام، أي: حضَرتها ودخلتها، بخلاف غيرهم، فإنّه لا يدخُلُها إلا يَومَ القيامة، أو لأنَّ الله وملائكته شهدا لهـ بالموافاة. (١) - وقال ابن الأنباري: لأن الله وملائكته يشهدون له بالجنة، فمعنى شهيد: مشهود له. وقيل: لأنه يشهد عند خروج روحه ما له من الثواب والكرامة، وقيل: لأن عليه شاهدا وهو دمه، فإنه يبعث وجرحه يثعب دما، وقيل: لسقوطه على الأرض والأرض شاهدة وشهيد على وزن فعيل بمعنى فاعل، أي شاهد لدار السلام، وقيل: بمعنى مفعول أي مشهود له.
They were called shuhada' (martyrs) because their souls witnessed (shahidat) Dar al-Salam (the Abode of Peace), i.e., they attended and entered it, unlike others, for they do not enter it except on the Day of Resurrection; or because Allah and His angels testified for him with the fulfillment (of reward). (1) - And Ibn al-Anbari said: Because Allah and His angels testify for him with Paradise, so the meaning of shahid is mashhud lahu (one for whom testimony is given). And it is said: Because he witnesses at the departure of his soul what he has of reward and honor. And it is said: Because there is a witness against him, which is his blood, for he is resurrected while his wound gushes blood. And it is said: Because of his falling to the ground while the earth is a witness. And shahid is on the pattern of fa'il meaning fa'il (active), i.e., a witness to Dar al-Salam; and it is said: on the pattern of maf'ul (passive), i.e., mashhud lahu (one for whom testimony is given).
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage explains the multiple interpretations of why martyrs (shuhada') are called by that name. The author begins by stating that the term shuhada' is derived from 'witnessing' (shuhud): their souls have witnessed Dar al-Salam (Paradise) by entering it immediately upon death, unlike other believers who only enter on the Day of Resurrection. Alternatively, it is because Allah and His angels testify for the martyr with the promised reward (al-muwafah). The footnote (1) then provides additional linguistic and exegetical explanations: Ibn al-Anbari's view that shahid means mashhud lahu (one for whom testimony is given), that the martyr himself witnesses his reward at death, that his blood is a witness against him, that the earth witnesses his fall, and the morphological possibility that shahid is either active (witness) or passive (witnessed for). The passage thus shows the richness of the term's theological and linguistic dimensions.

شهداء
دار السلام
الموافاة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The term 'shahid' only means 'martyr' in the sense of one killed in battle.
Correction: The passage shows that 'shahid' linguistically means 'witness' and is applied to martyrs for multiple reasons, including their immediate entry into Paradise or being testified for by Allah and angels.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The term 'shahid' is rich in meaning, rooted in the concept of witnessing, and is applied to martyrs for multiple theological and linguistic reasons.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The martyr's soul witnesses Paradise immediately. If your soul were to leave your body at this moment, what would it witness? Are you living in such a way that your heart already perceives the reality of Dar al-Salam?
?
Ibn al-Anbari said 'shahid' can mean 'one for whom testimony is given.' On the Day of Judgment, who will testify for you? How are you ensuring that your deeds, your blood, and your very existence will speak for you, not against you?
?
The passage shows that the earth itself is a witness for the martyr. Consider your own actions: if the ground you walk on could speak, what would it say about you? Are you aware that every place you tread is a witness to your faith or your negligence?

The Giving of Books: Process and Special Honors
Narrative of book distribution and special honors.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the process by which the books of deeds are given on Judgment Day and the special honors of Abu Bakr and Umar.

Core Idea
The giving of books is a detailed event with signs for believers and disbelievers.

This passage from Imam Dardir describes the eschatological event of the distribution of records. It begins with the compilation of deeds into a single scroll, stored under the Throne, then brought by a wind to each person. The angels hand the book according to one's faith—believers receive with the right hand, disbelievers with the left. The text also highlights the unique positions of Abu Bakr and Umar.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the sequential nature of the description.
2
Identify the stages of the process
List the steps: compilation, storage under the Throne, wind bringing scrolls to necks, angels handing them over, and the final hand (right or left).
3
Reflect on the special honors
Notice that Umar is the first to take his book with his right hand and has a radiance; Abu Bakr is the chief of those entering without reckoning. Ask yourself why they received these honors.
This connects to their high status in Islam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وحاصل ما قيل في ذلك: أنَّ صحائف الأيام والليالي توصل حتى تكون صحيفةً واحدةً، وقيل: يُنسَخُ ما في جميعها في صحيفة واحدة، فإذا ماتَ العَبدُ جُعِلتْ في خزانة تحت العرش، حتى إذا كان يَومُ القيامةِ والناسُ في الموقفِ بَعَثَ الله تعالى ريحا فتطيرها من تلك الخزانة، فلا تخطى صحيفةٌ عُنق صاحبها، ثُمَّ تَأخُذُها الملائكةُ مِنَ الأعناق فيعطونها لهم في أيديهم على حسب حالِهِم مِنْ إيمان أو كُفْرِ، فالمؤمنُ يعطى كتابه بيمينه، والكافرُ بشماله، ويثقَبُ  َصدرُه فيُدخِلُ يَدَه اليُسْرى فيه ويأخُذُ كِتابَه مِنْ وراءِ ظَهرِه. وأولُ مَنْ يَأخُذُ كِتابه بيمينه على الإطلاقِ عُمَرُ بنُ الخَطَّابِ رَضِي الله عنه وله شعاعٌ عَنْهُ كالشمس، وأما أبو بكر فهو رئيس السبعين ألفا الذين يدخلون الجنّةَ بغَيرِ حِساب. ثُمَّ إذا أَخَذَ العبدُ كِتابه وجدَ حُروفَه نيّرةً أو مُظْلِمةً على حسَبِ الأعمالِ الحسَنةِ أو القبيحةِ، وأَوّلُ خطّ فيها اقْرَأْ كِتَابَكَ كَفَىٰ بِنَفْسِكَ الْيَوْمَ عَلَيْكَ حَسِياً ) فإذا قرأهُ ابَضَ وجْهُه إنْ كان مؤمنا ، واسْوَدَّ إنْ كان كافرًا، وذلك قوله تعالى: ﴿يَوْ جوهٌ وَتَسْوَدُّ وُجُوهُ ) (۲) الآية . ويخلق الله تعالى له عِلْمَ القِراءةِ، وَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ يَقْرأُ فِي الدنيا. والصحيحُ : أنَّ عُصاة المؤمنين يأخُذون صحائفهم بأيمانهم، ويكون علامةً على دخولهم الجنَّةَ، ولو بعد دخولهم النار.
And the summary of what has been said about that: The scrolls of days and nights are connected until they become one scroll; and it is said: what is in all of them is copied into one scroll. So when the servant dies, they are placed in a treasury beneath the Throne, until when the Day of Resurrection comes and the people are in the station (maqif), Allah Almighty sends a wind that flies them from that treasury, and no scroll misses the neck of its owner. Then the angels take them from the necks and give them to them in their hands according to their state of belief or disbelief. So the believer is given his book in his right hand, and the disbeliever in his left, and his chest is pierced, and he inserts his left hand into it and takes his book from behind his back. And the first to take his book in his right hand absolutely is 'Umar ibn al-Khattab, may Allah be pleased with him, and he has a radiance from him like the sun. As for Abu Bakr, he is the chief of the seventy thousand who enter Paradise without reckoning. Then when the servant takes his book, he finds its letters bright or dark according to good or bad deeds. And the first line in it is: 'Read your book; sufficient is yourself today as a reckoner against you.' (17:14) So when he reads it, his face turns white if he is a believer, and black if he is a disbeliever, and that is the saying of the Exalted: 'On the day when faces are whitened and faces are blackened' (3:106). And Allah Almighty creates for him the knowledge of reading, even if he did not read in the world. And the correct view is that sinful believers take their scrolls in their right hands, and it is a sign of their entry into Paradise, even if after entering the Fire.
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage is a detailed narrative describing how the books (records of deeds) are given to people on Judgment Day. It begins by explaining the process of compilation: the daily scrolls are either joined into one scroll or copied into one. After death, the scroll is stored under the Throne. On Judgment Day, Allah sends a wind that brings each scroll to its owner's neck; angels then take them and hand them over according to the person's faith: believers receive with the right hand, disbelievers with the left (or from behind). The author then notes a special honor: 'Umar ibn al-Khattab is the first to take his book with his right hand absolutely, and he emits a radiant light. Abu Bakr is the chief of the seventy thousand who enter Paradise without reckoning. Next, the passage describes the state of the book itself: the letters appear bright or dark corresponding to good or evil deeds. The first words written in it are the verse 'Read your book...' (17:14). Upon reading, the believer's face whitens and the disbeliever's face blackens, as per Qur'an 3:106. Allah grants even the illiterate the ability to read that book. Finally, the correct position (al-sahih) is stated: sinful believers still receive their books in their right hands, which is a sign of eventual entry into Paradise even if they must enter the Fire first. The passage combines scriptural proof, traditional reports, and theological clarification.

Key Terms

الكتاب
يمين
شمال
عرش

Checkpoint
Who is the first person to take his book with his right hand on Judgment Day according to the passage?
A) Abu Bakr
B) 'Umar ibn al-Khattab
C) The Prophet Muhammad
D) 'Uthman ibn 'Affan

Key Takeaway
The giving of the book on Judgment Day is a detailed process that distinguishes believers and disbelievers, with special honors for Abu Bakr and Umar.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your book were handed to you today, which hand would it be placed in? What does that reveal about the state of your heart and your deeds right now?
?
Umar ibn al-Khattab will be the first to receive his book in his right hand, with a radiance like the sun. Are you living in a way that even hopes to be among those who receive their book easily? What specific habit or sin do you need to change today to prepare for that moment?
?
Abu Bakr leads the seventy thousand who enter Paradise without reckoning. Does your life reflect the kind of faith and certainty that frees you from the anxiety of scrutiny? What is one area where you are relying on your own deeds rather than on Allah's mercy to save you?

The Appearance of the Book and the Fate of Sinful Believers
Description of book content and ruling on sinful believers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the state of the book's content and the ruling that sinful believers still receive their books in their right hand as a sign of eventual Paradise.

Core Idea
The appearance of the book reflects deeds, and even sinful believers are honored with the right hand.

After receiving the book, the believer sees its letters bright or dark according to deeds. The first line is a Qur'anic verse, and the reader's face changes color. Allah grants the ability to read. The passage concludes with the correct view that sinful believers receive their books in the right hand, signifying their ultimate salvation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Pay attention to the contrast between bright and dark letters.
2
Analyze the state of the book and its effects
Notice that the letters appear bright for good deeds and dark for bad deeds. The first line is the Qur'anic verse 'Read your book...'. The reader's face whitens or blackens accordingly.
Consider why Allah creates reading ability for those who could not read in the world.
3
Understand the ruling on sinful believers
The passage ends with the correct view (al-sahih) that sinful believers receive their scrolls in their right hands. This is a sign of their eventual entry into Paradise, even if they must enter the Fire first.
This clarifies a common misunderstanding.

Types of Intercession of the Prophet
Lists and describes three types of intercession of the Prophet.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three types of intercession of the Prophet Muhammad and which are exclusive to him according to classical scholars.

Core Idea
Intercession is of three types, and not all are exclusive to the Prophet.

The doctrine of the Prophet's intercession (shafa'ah) is a key belief in Sunni Islam. In this passage, the author categorizes intercession into three distinct kinds, each with varying scholarly consensus on whether it is uniquely the Prophet's prerogative. This lesson unpacks each type and the evidence behind the differences of opinion.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice how the author lists three types with concise definitions.
The passage includes a brief linguistic note on the word 'shafa'ah'.
2
Identify the three types
Find each of the three types of intercession. Note the first two are said to be exclusive to the Prophet; the third is debated.
Pay attention to the scholars cited: al-Nawawi, Qadi 'Iyad, and others.
3
Understand the scholarly debate on exclusivity
For the third type, note that Qadi 'Iyad says it is not exclusive, al-Nawawi hesitated, and later scholars doubted. Ask yourself why this matters for theology.
The relied-upon view (al-mu'tamad) is that the third type is not exclusive.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
- وكالشفاعة(۳) وهي أنواع: الأَوَّلُ: شفاعته لها في فصل القضاء لإراحة الخلق مِنْ طولِ الوُقوفِ ومَشَقّتِه، وهي مختصة به. الثاني: شفاعته في إدخال قوم الجنة بغير حساب، قال النووي: وهي مختصة به. الثالثُ: الشفاعةُ فيمن استحَقَّ دُخول النارِ أنْ لا يَدْخُلَها، قال عياض: وليست خَاصَّةً به، وتردَّدَ النَّوَوِيُّ، أي لأنه لم يرد تصريح بذلك. (۱) سورة الإسراء: من الآية ١٤ (۳) له، من شفع (۲) سورة آل عمران: من الآية ١٠٦ الشفاعة من «الشفع» ضد الوتر، كأن الشافع ضم سؤاله إلى سؤال المشفوع يشفع، والمشفع بكسر الفاء الذي يقبل الشفاعة والمشفع - بفتحها الذي تقبل شفاعته. (٤) قاله النووي تبعا للقاضي عياض، وتردد ابن دقيق العيد في الاختصاص، وتبعه السبكي وابن جر قائلا: لا دليل عليه ومثله لا يدرك بالقياس والاجتهاد. [سباعي، ص ١٦٠] (٥) وهو المعتمد. [صاوي، ص۷۰] ، وتبعه ابن السبكي في جمع الجوامع. [سباعي، ص ١٦٠]
- And intercession (al-shafa'ah) (3) and it has types: The first: his intercession for the settling of judgment (fasl al-qada') to give the creation relief from the length of standing and its hardship, and it is exclusive to him. The second: his intercession for entering a people into Paradise without reckoning; al-Nawawi said: it is exclusive to him. The third: intercession for those who deserve entry into the Fire that they not enter it; 'Iyad said: it is not exclusive to him, and al-Nawawi hesitated, i.e., because no explicit statement has come regarding that. (1) Surah al-Isra': from verse 14, (3) from shafa'a, (2) Surah Al 'Imran: from verse 106. Al-shafa'ah is from al-shaf' (even) as opposed to al-witr (odd), as if the intercessor joins his request to the request of the one interceded for. Al-mushaffa' (with kasr of the fa') is the one who accepts intercession, and al-mushaffa' (with fatha) is the one whose intercession is accepted. (4) Al-Nawawi said it following al-Qadi 'Iyad, and Ibn Daqiq al-'Id hesitated about exclusivity, and al-Subki and Ibn Jar followed him saying: there is no evidence for it, and the like cannot be grasped by analogy or ijtihad. [Siba'i, p. 160] (5) And it is the relied-upon view. [Sawi, p. 70], and Ibn al-Subki followed him in Jam' al-Jawami'. [Siba'i, p. 160]
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage classifies the types of intercession (shafa'ah) of the Prophet Muhammad. It begins by noting that al-shafa'ah is derived from al-shaf' (even number), implying that the intercessor adds his plea to that of the person he intercedes for. Then it enumerates three types: (1) Intercession for the settling of judgment (fasl al-qada')—that is, to hasten the reckoning and give relief from the long wait in the station. The author states this is exclusive to the Prophet. (2) Intercession for entering a group into Paradise without any reckoning. Al-Nawawi is cited saying this is also exclusive to the Prophet. (3) Intercession for those who deserve the Fire to be spared from entering it. Here, Qadi 'Iyad says it is not exclusive, while al-Nawawi hesitated due to lack of explicit text. The footnote (4) adds scholarly discussion: Ibn Daqiq al-'Id, al-Subki, and Ibn Jar doubted exclusivity, and the relied-upon view (al-mu'tamad) is that it is not exclusive. The passage thus provides a clear taxonomy and indicates the degree of scholarly consensus on each type.

Key Terms
الشفاعة
شفاعة
محمد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All types of intercession are exclusive to the Prophet.
Correction: The passage shows that for the third type (sparing from Hell), there is a difference of opinion, and the relied-upon view is that it is not exclusive, as Qadi 'Iyad and later scholars held.

Checkpoint
Which type of intercession does the passage say is not necessarily exclusive to the Prophet?
A) Intercession for judgment
B) Intercession for entering Paradise without reckoning
C) Intercession for those deserving the Fire not to enter
D) All are exclusive

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's intercession is of three types, with only the first two being explicitly exclusive to him; the third type's exclusivity is debated.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you find yourself placing more hope in the Prophet's intercession than in your own deeds? How does the knowledge that the first two types are exclusive to the Prophet affect that hope—does it increase your reliance on his intercession or push you to work harder on your own actions?
?
If the third type of intercession is not exclusive to the Prophet, what does that tell you about the breadth of Allah's mercy? Are you comfortable relying solely on that mercy without striving to avoid deeds that warrant the Fire?
?
The Prophet (peace be upon him) will intercede to hasten the judgment and relieve the waiting. Does this thought give you comfort, or does it remind you of the intensity of that standing? How will you prepare for that moment starting today?
